# CLAUDE.md

This file provides guidance to Claude Code (claude.ai/code) when working with code in this repository.

## Project Overview
ComfyUI-Pixaroma is a custom-node plugin for ComfyUI: ~40 nodes plus canvas-wide tools, all under the `👑 Pixaroma` menu, with zero core dependencies (PIL + PyTorch come from ComfyUI's environment). The families:
- **Fullscreen editors:** 3D Builder, Paint Studio, Image Composer, Image Crop, AudioReact.
- **Prompt tools:** Prompt Multi / Pack / Stack / From List, Find and Replace, Show Text, Text, Prompt Reader.
- **Image I/O & resize:** Load Image, Preview Image, Save Mp4, Image Resize, Remove Background.
- **Layout & utility:** Resolution, Switch / Switch WH / Switch Source, Mute Switch, XY Plot, Number, WH, Notify, Version Check.
- **Annotation & overlay:** Note, Text Overlay, Text Watermark, Label, Compare.
- **Canvas-wide features (no node added):** Align, Node Colors, Brand defaults, Connection FX, Run Button FX.

Each node's behavior + invariants live in its own "Patterns (do not regress)" section below; the directory map and the Token-Saving table point you to the exact file per task.

## Development Setup
No build step. Install by placing this folder in `ComfyUI/custom_nodes/`. ComfyUI auto-imports `__init__.py` on startup.
No test suite or linting configuration exists in this project.

## Architecture

### Entry Points
- `__init__.py` — Aggregates all node classes, registers routes, exports `WEB_DIRECTORY = "./js"`
- `server_routes.py` — aiohttp HTTP routes for file I/O, asset serving, and AI features
- `nodes/*.py` — Individual node implementations (one per editor, all under 100 lines)

### Node → ComfyUI Integration
Each node file exports `NODE_CLASS_MAPPINGS` and `NODE_DISPLAY_NAME_MAPPINGS`. `__init__.py` merges them all.

Nodes are `OUTPUT_NODE = True` and receive editor state as a serialized JSON string inside a widget dict (`kwargs.get("SomeWidget")`). They load pre-rendered images from disk (written by the browser) and return PyTorch tensors.

### Frontend → Backend Data Flow
1. User edits in browser (WebGL / Canvas)
2. JS saves result to disk via `POST /pixaroma/api/*/save`
3. On workflow execution, Python node reads the saved file path from widget JSON and loads it as a tensor

### Backend Routes (server_routes.py)
| Route | Purpose |
|-------|---------|
| `/pixaroma/api/layer/upload` | Save paint layers |
| `/pixaroma/api/project/save` | Save composition |
| `/pixaroma/api/paint/save` | Save paint strokes |
| `/pixaroma/api/3d/save` | Save 3D render |
| `/pixaroma/api/3d/bg_upload` | Upload 3D background |
| `/pixaroma/api/crop/save` | Save crop result |
| `/pixaroma/api/preview/save` | Preview Image Pixaroma — write PNG with workflow metadata to ComfyUI `output/` with auto-increment counter (filename_prefix supports `subfolder/prefix`) |
| `/pixaroma/api/preview/prepare` | Preview Image Pixaroma — return JSON `{image_b64, suggested_filename}` with workflow metadata embedded; suggested_filename peeks the next free counter for Save-to-Disk |
| `/pixaroma/remove_bg` | AI background removal (rembg) |
| `/pixaroma/assets/{filename}` | Serve logo/assets |
| `/pixaroma/api/note/icons/list` | List inline-icon SVGs in `assets/icons/note/` |

### Frontend Directory Structure
The frontend is organized into **directory-per-editor** modules under `js/`. Each directory is self-contained with files split by concern (~300 lines max per file).

**File extension convention:** Only `index.js` files (entry points that call `app.registerExtension`) use the `.js` extension. All other module files use `.mjs`. This is because ComfyUI auto-loads every `*.js` file as a separate extension — using `.mjs` for non-entry modules prevents them from being loaded twice.

```
js/   (only index.js entry points use .js; every other module is .mjs so ComfyUI does not double-load it)

framework/   Shared UI toolkit - EVERY editor depends on this, so edit with care:
  index.mjs (barrel, import from here) | theme.mjs (CSS + BRAND #f66744 + _uiIcon) | layout.mjs (createEditorLayout fullscreen shell) | components.mjs (buttons/sliders/inputs/zoom/transform) | layers.mjs (layer panel) | canvas.mjs (canvas settings/toolbar/drag-drop) | fonts.mjs (font registry + custom drop-in fonts) | text_render.mjs (canvas mirror of nodes/_text_render_helpers.py) | text_editor.mjs (shared text-props panel: default / composerMode / watermarkMode) | bg_removal_dropdown.mjs (shared AI Remove-BG picker)

shared/   Shared utilities + Nodes 2.0 helpers:
  utils.mjs (BRAND, hideJsonWidget, installFocusTrap) | preview.mjs (ResizeObserver mini-previews) | help.mjs (Help popup + registerNodeHelp/getNodeHelp registry, convention #16) | color_picker.mjs (Pixaroma Color Picker: compact + live-preview) | nodes2.mjs (applyAdaptiveCanvasOnly, isVueNodes, canvasBackingScale, installZoomRepaint) | graph_undo_guard.mjs (blocks Ctrl+Z escape, Vue Compat #6) | graph_loading.mjs (isGraphLoading, Vue Compat #19) | queue_drivers.mjs (shared lock for queue-driver nodes) | resize_floor.mjs + resize_panel.mjs (Nodes 2.0 resize floor + shared resize-mode panel / makeNumericInput) | index.mjs, label_css.mjs

Canvas-wide features (patch the canvas, add NO node):
  brand/index.js         Brand dark defaults for ANY node whose CATEGORY starts "👑 Pixaroma" (do NOT re-add per-node color guards)
  node_colors/index.js   Right-click Node/Group color palette popup (favorites, copy/paste); presets in HUE_FOLDERS (see Vue Compat #20)
  connection_fx/index.js Pixaroma.Connection.FX - wire-drag magnets + connect sparkles
  run_button_fx/index.js Pixaroma.RunButton.FX - Run-button visual effects
  align/index.js         Pixaroma.Align.* - smart-snap + alignment guides
  help_toolbar/index.js  Pixaroma.HelpToolbar - the orange ? Help button in the node selection toolbar (convention #16); per-node help content lives in the sibling help_defs.mjs

Fullscreen editors (class + mixin pattern, see "Mixin Pattern" below; core.mjs = shell, sibling .mjs add prototype methods, index.js wires it):
  paint/        PaintStudio: core canvas render transform events tools history ui engine api
  3d/           Pixaroma3DEditor (Three.js vendored, see Offline-first): core engine objects shapes shape_params composites picker importer interaction persistence api
  composer/     PixaromaEditor (+ FX-grade + text layers): core eraser crop placeholder render ui layers fx_engine api
  crop/         CropEditor: core interaction render panel alignments
  note/         NoteEditor (rich-text): core toolbar blocks render sanitize css codeview icons
  audio_studio/ AudioStudioEditor (WebGL): core transport audio_analysis render shaders ui api
  label/        Title-less DOM label + fullscreen editor: core render

Switch family (per-renderer split; Nodes 2.0 = DOM row list, Vue Compat #16/#17):
  switch/ (N-to-1 router: core render editor vue_list) | mute_switch/ (toggle branches via PIXAROMA_MUTE_CHAIN: core render editor upstream vue_list) | switch_source/ (A/B banks: core editor) | switch_wh/ (fixed A/B W-H)

Prompt + text nodes:
  prompt_stack/ prompt_multi/ prompt_pack/ (each: core render interaction) | find_replace/ (core render interaction) | text/ showtext/ prompt_reader/

Image I/O + resize (load_image + image_resize paint INPUT->OUTPUT cards in onDrawForeground):
  load_image/ (ui panel_polish resize_modes api) | image_resize/ (ui) | preview/ | save_mp4/ | pause_image/ (state ui)

Overlay / annotation / utility:
  text_overlay/ (core interaction defaults) + text_watermark/ (defaults) share framework/text_editor.mjs + nodes/_text_render_helpers.py | compare/ | resolution/ | xy_plot/ (core ui grid - 3rd queue-driver -> grid PNG) | reference/ | notify/ | number/ | wh/ | version_check/ (Nodes 2.0 diagnostic node)
```

### Mixin Pattern (how editor classes are split)
Editor classes (PaintStudio, Pixaroma3DEditor, PixaromaEditor, CropEditor) use a **prototype mixin pattern** to split methods across files:
- `core.mjs` defines the class with constructor and UI building
- Other `.mjs` files add methods: `ClassName.prototype.methodName = function() { ... };`
- `index.js` imports all mixin files as **side-effect imports** before using the class
- All methods use `this` — they have full access to the instance

### Import Conventions
- Editors import framework from `../framework/index.mjs`
- Editors import shared utils from `../shared/index.mjs`
- ComfyUI app is imported as `import { app } from "/scripts/app.js";` (absolute) or relative `../../../../scripts/app.js`
- Only `index.js` entry points use `.js` extension; all other modules use `.mjs`

### Editor Isolation
Each editor directory is a self-contained sub-project. When working on a specific editor, **only read and modify files in that editor's directory** (e.g. `js/paint/*.mjs` and `nodes/node_paint.py`). The only shared dependencies across all editors are `js/framework/` and `js/shared/` — be cautious modifying these as changes affect every editor.

### ComfyUI Vue Frontend Compatibility
ComfyUI's new Vue 3 frontend introduces several behavioral differences from the legacy LiteGraph frontend. These patterns were discovered during debugging and must be followed:

1. **`onDrawForeground` does not fire** — The Vue frontend does not call LiteGraph rendering hooks. Use `setInterval` polling instead for detecting upstream changes (see `js/composer/index.js` for the polling pattern).

2. **Editor overlay removal** — Vue may remove editor overlay elements from the DOM without triggering close callbacks. Always use the `isEditorOpen(node)` pattern that checks `overlay.isConnected` rather than trusting `node._pixaromaEditor` references:
   ```js
   function isEditorOpen(node) {
     if (!node._pixaromaEditor) return false;
     const overlay = node._pixaromaEditor.overlay;
     if (!overlay || !overlay.isConnected) {
       node._pixaromaEditor = null;
       return false;
     }
     return true;
   }
   ```

3. **`graph.links` may be a Map** — In newer ComfyUI versions, `graph.links` can be a `Map` instead of a plain object. Always try both access patterns:
   ```js
   let link = graph.links?.[linkId];
   if (!link && typeof graph.links?.get === "function") link = graph.links.get(linkId);
   ```

4. **Execution detection** — Use ComfyUI API events (`execution_start`, `executing` with `null` detail = finished) imported from `/scripts/api.js`. These are the reliable way to detect workflow execution completion.

5. **DOM widget may be nulled while editor is open** — Vue can tear down a node's DOM widget (added via `node.addDOMWidget`) while the fullscreen editor overlay is still showing. If the editor's `onSave` callback caches a `widget` reference in a closure, that reference becomes null and `widget.value = ...` throws. Guard with null-check + re-lookup from `node.widgets`:
   ```js
   editor.onSave = (jsonStr, dataURL) => {
     sceneJson = jsonStr;
     const w = widget || node.widgets?.find((x) => x.name === "SceneWidget");
     if (w) w.value = { scene_json: jsonStr };
   };
   ```

6. **Ctrl+Z escapes editor overlays to the graph** — The Vue frontend's undo is driven by `changeTracker.undo` (in the workflow store), which calls `app.loadGraphData` → `graph.configure` → `graph.clear`. `window.addEventListener("keydown", fn, true)` + `stopImmediatePropagation` does NOT preempt it because `changeTracker.undo` is scheduled via `requestAnimationFrame` from a different code path, and patching `app.graph.undo` / `Comfy.Undo` command doesn't cover it either. The only reliable block is patching the bottleneck functions while the editor is open, then restoring them on cleanup:
   ```js
   this._savedLoadGraphData = app.loadGraphData.bind(app);
   app.loadGraphData = () => Promise.resolve();
   this._savedGraphConfigure = app.graph.configure.bind(app.graph);
   app.graph.configure = () => {};
   // On cleanup: app.loadGraphData = this._savedLoadGraphData; etc.
   ```
   See `js/note/core.mjs` for the full pattern (also neuters `graph.undo/redo`, `Comfy.Undo`/`Comfy.Redo` commands, plus a `node.onRemoved` resurrection-close safety net). Always debug this class of bug with a stack trace from `onRemoved` — it will show you the exact path that needs wrapping.

   **CRITICAL — the patches MUST self-heal, or the editor can BRICK the whole UI.** Per Vue Compat #2 the overlay can be torn down WITHOUT the editor's cleanup running (e.g. closing the workflow tab while the editor is open). If that happens, `app.loadGraphData` stays a no-op forever and the user can no longer open OR create ANY workflow until they refresh the page (confirmed May 2026 via console: `app.loadGraphData.toString()` stuck at `() => Promise.resolve()` with zero overlays in the DOM). Restoring only in `close()`/`_cleanup` is NOT enough. Make the patched functions self-restoring: when called while the overlay is gone (`!overlay.isConnected`) or after close, restore the originals and pass the call through. Ctrl+Z while the editor is genuinely open is still blocked (overlay alive → early return). Reference implementation: `js/text_overlay/core.mjs` `_overlayAlive()` + `_restoreGraphPatches()` wired into the patched `app.loadGraphData`/`app.graph.configure`. Any editor using this neutering pattern (Text Overlay done; **Image Composer done** - `js/composer/core.mjs` `_installGraphPatches()` / `_restoreGraphPatches()` / `_overlayAlive()`, installed in `ui.mjs build()`, restored in `interaction.mjs _cleanupKeys` + `index.js isEditorOpen` teardown, with a stale-patch re-entrancy guard since the Composer re-instantiates per open; **Note and AudioReact still need it**) must follow the self-heal approach. Symptom that it's missing (Composer, May 2026): once the editor's OWN undo stack is exhausted, the next Ctrl+Z escapes and reverts graph actions (e.g. removes the node on the canvas) - the editor capturing Ctrl+Z + preventDefault is NOT enough because the Vue undo runs via rAF through loadGraphData.

   **UPDATE (May 2026): this neutering is now ONE shared helper — `js/shared/graph_undo_guard.mjs` `installGraphUndoGuard(isAlive)`. Do NOT hand-roll a new per-editor patch; use the shared guard.** It is refcount-safe (multiple editors open at once — fixes the two-editor FIFO-close brick that the single-global-slot per-editor copies had), self-healing (restores on overlay teardown), and covers the FULL set: `loadGraphData`, `graph.configure`, `graph.undo`/`redo`, AND the `Comfy.Undo`/`Comfy.Redo` command-store dispatch (the old per-editor copies missed undo/redo + the command store, so Ctrl+Z via the Vue command path could still escape). EVERY fullscreen editor now uses it — **Paint, 3D Builder, Image Crop, Image Composer, Note, AudioReact, Text Overlay** (Text Overlay migrated May 2026 — it was the last holdout on a hand-rolled loadGraphData/configure-only patch that missed undo/redo + the command store) — by calling `this._undoGuardOff = installGraphUndoGuard(() => this._overlayAlive())` (or `() => !!this.el.overlay?.isConnected`) when the overlay mounts, and `this._undoGuardOff?.(); this._undoGuardOff = null;` on teardown. Route the uninstall through `layout.onCleanup` (NOT only the ✕ button's `_close`) so the Save-auto-close, ✕, and node-removal paths ALL uninstall exactly once; also call it from a wrapped `node.onRemoved` so deleting the node mid-edit restores the originals + releases resources (3D's WebGL contexts, listeners). Add a double-open guard on each "Open …" button (`if (isEditorOpen(node)) return;`) since the guard assumes one editor instance per node. The earlier per-editor descriptions in this paragraph are historical — they were all migrated to the shared helper.

7. **`installFocusTrap` and contenteditable don't mix** — Paint/Composer/3D call `installFocusTrap(overlay)` so their hidden textarea absorbs focus for keyboard-shortcut isolation. For rich-text editors that use a contenteditable (Note Pixaroma), do NOT call `installFocusTrap`: its `mouseup` handler refocuses the hidden textarea whenever the event target isn't INPUT/TEXTAREA/SELECT, which steals focus on every toolbar-button click (user has to re-click into the editor to type) and wipes the text selection when a drag-select ends outside the panel. Use the `loadGraphData` / `graph.configure` neutering pattern from point 6 instead.

8. **`nodeCreated` fires BEFORE `configure()` — defer initial DOM widget population via `queueMicrotask`** — In Vue's new frontend, the extension-level `nodeCreated(node)` hook fires DURING node construction, BEFORE ComfyUI calls `configure(data)` to restore saved widget values. If you render the DOM widget contents synchronously inside `nodeCreated`, you render from the Python default and then flash to the saved state when `onConfigure`'s re-render hook fires milliseconds later. The fix: create an empty `root` div, call `addDOMWidget(..., root, ...)`, wire event listeners, cache `node._xxxRoot = root`, and **defer the initial populate to `queueMicrotask(() => { ... })`** so the restored widget value is visible by the time we read it. Keep the `onConfigure` re-render for the "open a different workflow into an already-constructed node" case. Pattern applies to any hidden-JSON-widget node (Resolution Pixaroma is the reference implementation; Note Pixaroma's timing happens to mask the flash because its initial render is visually lighter). Full diagnostic path: add `console.log` of the widget value in both `nodeCreated` setup and `onConfigure` — if the first shows defaults and the second shows the saved value, you have this bug.

9. **For hidden state, prefer Python `hidden` inputs + `node.properties` + `graphToPrompt` over hidden STRING widgets — eliminates both the input dot and the persistence fragility.** Vue auto-exposes primitive-type *required* inputs (STRING/INT/FLOAT) as convertible input slots that flash a grey dot on hover. Two ways to suppress the dot:
   - **Wrong**: `node.removeInput(idx)` on the auto-created slot. Causes saved JSON to have `"inputs": []`, and on workflow RELOAD Vue fails to reconnect the saved `widgets_values[0]` to the hidden STRING widget — silent revert to defaults on every workflow open.
   - **Right (Resolution Pixaroma pattern)**: Define the input as `"hidden"` (not `"required"`) in Python — no widget, no slot, no dot. Store state on `node.properties[YOUR_KEY]` (LiteGraph serializes `properties` natively in workflow JSON). At extension scope, monkey-patch `app.graphToPrompt` to inject the saved state into each node's `inputs.YourHiddenName` right before submission. Read state via `node.properties[YOUR_KEY]` in setup; include a one-time migration that scans `node.widgets_values` for the old JSON format if you're upgrading from a widget-based architecture.
   - **Acceptable (Note Pixaroma pattern)**: keep the required STRING widget + `hideJsonWidget`. The hover dot remains but persistence is rock-solid via the standard widget value flow. Use this when no extra prompt-time injection is desired.

10. **Custom widget click routing uses `computeSize` bounds, NOT actual rendered area.** LiteGraph's `processNodeWidgets` hit-tests clicks against `widget.last_y + widget.computeSize(width)[1]`. If a widget reports a small constant (e.g. `[width, 220]` matching native PreviewImage's `minHeight: 220`) but DRAWS at a larger height (e.g. `node.size[1] - y` for a "fill remaining space" widget), clicks below the `computeSize` line are NOT routed to `widget.mouse()` — they fall through to `node.onMouseDown`. This bites any node whose last widget needs to grow with the node body (preview strip, video preview, etc.). Two fixes: (a) DUAL CLICK PATH — extract click logic into a shared helper, call from BOTH `widget.mouse()` AND `nodeType.prototype.onMouseDown` so clicks anywhere over the rendered area work (Preview Image Pixaroma pattern); (b) make `computeSize` return the dynamic height (requires caching `_node` reference and computing the strip's own y from sibling widgets — complex and fragile). (a) is preferred.

11. **Preview state persistence across Vue workflow tab switching: `node.properties` + restore via `queueMicrotask(onNodeCreated)` AND `onConfigure`.** Vue's tab switching can tear down node UI state (anything in `node._xxx` instance fields). Anything that should survive — selected frame, expanded mode, frame URLs — must live on `node.properties` (LiteGraph serializes this natively). Build a `restoreFromProperties(node)` helper that re-hydrates the runtime state from properties; wire it from BOTH `queueMicrotask(() => restoreFromProperties(this))` in `onNodeCreated` (Compat #8 — fires after configure resolves the saved property values) AND `nodeType.prototype.onConfigure` (belt-and-braces). Idempotent via early-return on already-populated state. See "Preview Image Pixaroma Patterns" #4 for the full pattern — reuse it for any preview-style node where users would lose state when switching tabs.

12. **Read `app.canvas.graph_mouse` inside `draw()` for free per-frame hover detection on canvas-painted controls.** LiteGraph already redraws the node on every pointermove; any state computed in `draw` is implicitly per-frame. Convert mouse to node-local: `mx = graph_mouse[0] - node.pos[0]`. Hit-test against the same rect the click handler uses. Branch fill/stroke style on hover. No DOM widget needed — this is what native PreviewImage does for its X close button.

15. **Internal widgets (custom and DOM) need `canvasOnly: true` or they render in the Parameters tab and corrupt node-body layout.** The Vue frontend's right-sidebar Parameters tab iterates `node.widgets` and renders each one in the panel column. ALL Pixaroma editor nodes were affected: Paint (`PaintWidget`), Image Composer (`ComposerWidget`), Image Crop (`CropPanel` + `CropWidget`), 3D Builder (`SceneWidget`), Resolution (`resolution_ui`), Note (`note_dom`), Show Text (`text`), Save Mp4 (`pixaroma_video_preview`), Preview Image Pixaroma (`pixaroma_buttons` + `pixaroma_strip`), and Reference (`CounterWidget`). Two compounding bugs: (a) each canvas-painted internal widget appeared as a duplicated row in the Parameters tab — wrong, they're not user inputs; (b) each Parameters-panel `draw()` call wrote stale state with Parameters-panel-context coords (e.g. node._pixaromaCells in Preview Image Pixaroma) which the node body's own draw then read, reflowing/breaking the visible layout. Fix is the bundle's standard exclusion flag — set `canvasOnly: true` in the widget's options. Two surfaces: for `addCustomWidget`, the flag goes inside `options: { canvasOnly: true }` because Comfy reads `widget.options?.canvasOnly`; for `addDOMWidget(name, type, element, opts)`, the 4th arg IS the options object, so put `canvasOnly: true` directly there alongside `serialize`, `getMinHeight`, etc. Filter found in the bundle: `t.filter(e => !(e.options?.canvasOnly || e.options?.hidden || e.options?.advanced && !n.value))`. Always set this on new internal widgets; `serialize: false` alone is not enough (it only stops the value being saved into the workflow JSON, not the panel rendering).

14. **Info-panel descriptions render as PLAIN TEXT, not Markdown — verified empirically May 2026.** ComfyUI's frontend bundles a markdown renderer (`markdownRendererUtil-*.js` exporting `renderMarkdownToHtml`, GFM via `marked` + DOMPurify), and a code-trace agent identified `Ao(a)` call sites in `dialogService-*.js` that looked like the node Description used it. Empirically that's WRONG for the right-sidebar **Info** tab on a selected node: `**bold**`, `### headings`, `` `code` `` spans, `- bullets`, and `\n\n` paragraph breaks ALL appear as literal characters. Whitespace including `\n\n` is collapsed to a single space. The markdown renderer in the bundle is used elsewhere (e.g. `WidgetMarkdown`, the About panel, dialog content). For DESCRIPTION text in `class.DESCRIPTION` and per-input `tooltip` fields, write **concise plain prose** with complete-sentence punctuation; do not waste authoring effort on markdown markers. The hover tooltip on the node body itself does honour `white-space: pre-wrap` so `\n` line breaks survive there, but markdown markers still render literally. Bug class this prevents: spending an iteration loop trying to make `**bold**` work in the Info panel.

13. **`node.onResize` does not reliably fire for DOM-widget resizes — use `ResizeObserver`.** Same family as Compat #1 (`onDrawForeground` not firing): the Vue frontend handles many node-resize paths without invoking `node.onResize`, and even when it does the timing relative to DOM layout is inconsistent. Anything that needs to track the rendered size of a DOM widget (e.g. keeping a preview box square via `height = offsetWidth`) should attach a `ResizeObserver` to the element directly. ResizeObserver fires for every actual size change regardless of cause (node resize, container reflow, tab switch, parent layout shifts) and is supported in every browser ComfyUI runs in. Reference implementation: `js/shared/preview.mjs` — the `createNodePreview` helper used by Paint, Crop, Composer, and 3D Builder mini-previews. Bug class this prevents: "preview box renders as a wide rectangle and only snaps square after the user runs a workflow" (an old `requestAnimationFrame` 60-frame loop + `node.onResize` override would lock the height at the first measured width and never update on subsequent resizes).

16. **Per-slot UI aligned with input dots requires `onDrawForeground` + `onMouseDown` on `nodeType.prototype`, NOT custom widgets.** When you need to paint controls (toggles, buttons, badges) on the SAME horizontal line as each input slot dot, the Image Compare pattern is the only one that works in this ComfyUI/LiteGraph fork. Reference: `js/compare/index.js`. Things that DO NOT work and waste time if attempted:
    - **Custom canvas widgets per row** (via `node.addCustomWidget`): widgets render in the widget area BELOW the slot area, never aligned with slot dots. LG passes widgets a `y` parameter that's after the slot rows.
    - **`slot.pos = [x, y]` from inside `widget.draw`**: causes a layout feedback loop. Each draw shifts slot.pos, which shifts `computeSize`, which shifts the widget Y, which shifts slot.pos again. The node grows infinitely tall.
    - **`slot.pos` set once via stable index math**: doesn't visually align with anything you draw separately (the slot dot moves but your widget doesn't follow).
    - **`node.getConnectionPos` override**: per runtime probing (May 2026), this ComfyUI fork does NOT call `getConnectionPos` for the slot dot position. The override is silently bypassed. (See `calculateInputSlotPosFromSlot` in the bundle — it reads `slot.pos` first, defaults to internal vertical-stack math otherwise. Wires use a different path that DOES call getConnectionPos, but the dot itself doesn't.)

    What WORKS: leave native LG to position dots in its default top-stacked column. Patch `nodeType.prototype.onDrawForeground` (yes, it DOES fire reliably for paint despite Compat #1's note - that note is about specific hook tear-down paths, not about every render) and paint your per-slot UI AT each dot's Y. Patch `nodeType.prototype.onMouseDown` for clicks; hit-test the same rects you painted.

    Slot Y math that aligns exactly: `Y = TOP_PAD + (i - 1) * NODE_SLOT_HEIGHT + NODE_SLOT_HEIGHT/2` where `TOP_PAD = 4`, `NODE_SLOT_HEIGHT = 20`. Image Compare uses these values; Switch Pixaroma reuses them. Suppress the native input slot LABEL (not name — name is the Python kwarg key) by setting `slot.label = "​"` (zero-width space, U+200B); empty string `""` falls through the `||` chain back to `slot.name`. See `js/compare/index.js` for a working canvas-paint-on-input-row example and `js/switch/` for one that ALSO grows/shrinks the input list dynamically and handles per-row mutex toggle state.

    Bug class this prevents: spending 5+ commits trying to make custom widgets align with slot dots, only to discover the entire approach is wrong for this LG fork.

17. **`LGraphNode.configure()` fires `onConnectionsChange` for every connected slot during workflow load and Ctrl+Z undo. Any patched `onConnectionsChange` handler that mutates node state WILL have that state overwritten on every load.** Verified empirically in `api-D9vMMk51.js` step 5 of configure: `this.onConnectionsChange?.(M.INPUT, idx, true, link, slot)` is called for EVERY input slot that has a saved link. Bug class this causes: a custom node that auto-activates the just-connected row inside `handleConnect` (`state.activeIndex = slotIdx`) will see its saved active selection silently overwritten to whichever slot LG happens to restore last during configure replay. Same risk for anything else stored on `node.properties` that `handleConnect` / `handleDisconnect` writes.

    The fix is a configuring-flag gate. Set `node._<nodeId>Configuring = true` at the start of the patched `onConfigure` (before `_origConfigure.apply`), clear it in a `finally` block after the state-restore call returns, and in `onConnectionsChange` skip the user-intent state-mutation calls when the flag is true:

    ```js
    nodeType.prototype.onConfigure = function (info) {
      this._pixSwitchConfiguring = true;
      try {
        const r = _origConfigure?.apply(this, arguments);
        restoreFromProperties(this);  // synchronous; properties already merged in step 3
        return r;
      } finally {
        this._pixSwitchConfiguring = false;
      }
    };

    nodeType.prototype.onConnectionsChange = function (type, slotIndex, isConnected, link, ioSlot) {
      if (type === INPUT && !this._pixSwitchConfiguring) {
        if (isConnected && ioSlot?.link != null) handleConnect(this, slotIndex + 1);
        else if (!isConnected) handleDisconnect(this, slotIndex + 1);
      }
      return _origOnConnectionsChange?.apply(this, arguments);
    };
    ```

    The `try/finally` matters because `restoreFromProperties` (or anything that paints, dispatches sub-events, etc) might throw; without `finally` the flag would stick true forever and live user wires would silently no-op on the affected node. Reference: `js/switch/index.js` for the working implementation, plus Switch WH and Resolution which have NO `onConnectionsChange` handler at all (they have fixed slots, not dynamic) and are inherently immune to this bug. LiteGraph's configure does MERGE `data.properties` into `this.properties` key-by-key (step 3 in the bundle) so saved property values ARE restored correctly; the silent corruption comes purely from the post-restore connection-replay step.

    Bug class this prevents: every save+reload of the affected node resets state.activeIndex (or whatever else `handleConnect` mutates) to a deterministic-but-wrong value (usually the last connected slot in iteration order, not the user's saved choice). User-visible: "save with row 2 active, reload, row 1 is active. Other workflows also got reset somehow." If you hear that, look at whether the node's `onConnectionsChange` handler mutates state without a configuring-flag gate.

18. **Mutating SERIALIZED node state during the load/configure window falsely flags the workflow "modified" - just opening then closing a workflow pops the "Save Changes?" prompt with no edits.** ComfyUI's Vue change-tracker decides a workflow is dirty by serializing the graph and diffing against the saved JSON. Serialized state includes `node.size`, `node.inputs`/`node.outputs` (slot count, names, labels, types), `node.properties`, `node.widgets_values`, `node.flags`. If `onNodeCreated`, its deferred `queueMicrotask`/`requestAnimationFrame`, OR `onConfigure` (all of which run on a plain open) writes any of those to a value that differs from what was saved, the workflow is flagged modified. This bit FOUR nodes (issue #39, May 2026): **Text Overlay, Prompt Stack, Prompt Multi, Switch**. Two distinct mechanisms:
    - **Auto-resize on load** (Text Overlay `refreshTextLock` → `computeSize()`; Prompt Stack / Prompt Multi `rerender()` → `requestAnimationFrame(growNodeToContent)`). The deferred resize fires AFTER the change-tracker snapshots the loaded state, and the recomputed height differs from the saved `node.size[1]` by 1-2px (DOM/font measurement rounding) - so it rewrites `node.size` and dirties. Fix: do NOT resize on the load path; trust the saved `node.size` (it already fits, and `getMinHeight` enforces the floor). Only resize on genuine user actions (add/delete/toggle/typing/real wire change). Implementations: Text Overlay gates `refreshTextLock(node, allowResize)` behind a `_textOverlayConfiguring` flag (set in `onConfigure`, so the configure-replay of `onConnectionsChange` per Compat #17 doesn't resize); Prompt Stack / Multi expose a DOM-only `_pixPsRenderOnly` / `_pixPmRenderOnly` used by `onConfigure` + the initial render, while the grow path stays on the user-action handlers.
    - **Structural rewrite on load** (Switch `normalizeSlots` rewriting slot names/labels, `node.size`, and resetting `node.outputs[0].type` to `"*"`). On a clean load the saved slots already match, so every one of those writes is a needless mutation; the type reset is worst because the upstream link isn't resolved yet during configure, so a saved `IMAGE` type gets clobbered to `"*"`. Fix: make every write idempotent (only write when the value actually differs); resize only when the slot COUNT actually changed (track length before/after the trim/append loops); and in `updateOutputType`, never downgrade to `"*"` when the active slot IS wired but its upstream type can't be resolved yet (load race) - clear to `"*"` only when there's genuinely no active connection.

    The clean comparison node is **Prompt Pack**: its `onConfigure` only does `restoreFromProperties` + `applyState` (DOM only), never touches `node.size`/`inputs`/`outputs`, and its `getMinHeight` is a constant - so it never dirties. **Rule for any new node:** the load path (`onNodeCreated` + its deferred callbacks + `onConfigure`) must be a no-op against serialized state for an unchanged saved workflow. Verify by opening a saved workflow with your node and closing it - if "Save Changes?" appears with no edits, something on the load path is writing serialized state. (`node.setDirtyCanvas(true, true)` is just a canvas REDRAW flag and does NOT trip the change-tracker - Prompt Pack calls it on load and stays clean.)

    **`getMinHeight`/`getMaxHeight` tied to a LIVE DOM measurement is itself a dirty source — Text Overlay needed a FIXED constant height to fully fix it (May 2026).** Gating the auto-resize (above) was necessary but NOT sufficient for Text Overlay, because its DOM widget returned `measureContentHeight()` from `getMinHeight`/`getMaxHeight`, and LiteGraph uses those to drive `node.size`. The live measurement comes back a few px different between save and reload (font/layout sub-pixel timing — observed `node.size.1` going 458→472, 470→472), so `node.size` changed on every load → dirty. Attempts that ALSO failed: (a) a sticky tolerance anchored to `node.size[1]` — wrong units (total node height vs widget-content height) and the gap exceeded the tolerance anyway; (b) persisting the measured height in `node.properties` — the deferred capture stored it in a `requestAnimationFrame` AFTER `node.size` was already computed from a different measurement, so the stored height (414) and saved size (458) disagreed, AND adding the property added a key the saved baseline lacked. The ONLY robust fix was to remove measurement from the load path entirely: `getMinHeight`/`getMaxHeight` return a **hardcoded constant** (`BASE_H` + a fixed `HINT_H` when the text input is wired). A constant is byte-identical every save and load, so `node.size` can never differ → never dirty. Trade-off: if the panel's row layout changes, `BASE_H` must be updated by hand (there's a comment in `js/text_overlay/index.js` saying so). Prompt Stack / Prompt Multi avoid this trap a different way — their `getMinHeight` is also a live measurement but they have NO `getMaxHeight` and their saved `node.size` carries a buffer above the measurement, so `getMinHeight`'s jitter never exceeds the saved size and LiteGraph keeps the saved size unchanged. For a NEW DOM-widget node whose body height is essentially fixed, prefer a constant `getMinHeight` (like Prompt Pack); only use a live measurement if the content height genuinely varies, and then keep a buffer + no `getMaxHeight`.

    Separately, note that **ComfyUI restores your open workflow TABS on page reload** (a recently-closed tab can reappear once after Ctrl+F5 because the saved tab-list was captured before the close). That is core ComfyUI session-persistence, NOT a dirty-state or node bug - don't chase it as one.

19. **Connection restore fires `onConnectionsChange` at the GRAPH level AFTER each node's `onConfigure` returns - a per-node "configuring" flag does NOT cover it. Use the shared `isGraphLoading()` guard for any `onConnectionsChange` handler that mutates SERIALIZED state.** This is a sharper restatement of #17's failure mode, discovered when it bit THREE nodes (Switch issue #40, Image Resize, Crop - May 2026). The timing: `LGraph.configure` creates every node and calls each `node.configure` (which runs the `onConfigure` hook, where nodes set+clear a `_xxxConfiguring` flag), and THEN - after all nodes are configured - restores the saved LINKS, firing `onConnectionsChange(INPUT, idx, true, ...)` for each. By then every node's per-node configure flag is already cleared, so a handler that mutates serialized state on connect (Switch `handleConnect` -> `state.activeIndex = slotIdx`; Image Resize auto-swap -> `disconnectInput`; Crop -> `delete node.properties.pixaromaCropSource`) RUNS during the replay and overwrites the just-restored saved state. User-visible: the saved active row / wire / persisted source resets on every workflow open, tab switch, and Ctrl+Z undo. The per-node flag (#17) is necessary but NOT sufficient.

    The robust fix is a LOAD-WIDE guard: `js/shared/graph_loading.mjs` wraps `app.loadGraphData` (the single funnel for open / tab switch / Ctrl+Z) exactly once, holds a flag true for the whole load plus a 300ms trailing window (covering the link restore that settles a tick later), and exports `isGraphLoading()`. **Any `onConnectionsChange` handler that writes serialized state (`node.properties`, `node.size`, slots, `widgets_values`, an active index) MUST gate that write on `!isGraphLoading()`** (in addition to any per-node flag). Handlers that touch only NON-serialized runtime fields (a CSS class, `readOnly`, a transient `node._foo`, calling `renderUI` without writing properties/size) are safe and need no guard. Reference fixes: `js/switch/index.js`, `js/image_resize/index.js`, `js/crop/index.js`, `js/text_overlay/index.js` (defensive). NOTE: Switch + Image Resize still carry equivalent INLINE `loadGraphData` wraps (`_swLoadingGraph` / `_irLoadingGraph`) from before the shared helper existed - harmless (each wrap is idempotent via its own `app._pixXxLoadWrapped` flag), but new nodes should import `isGraphLoading()` rather than re-roll the wrap. Switch WH is inherently immune (fixed slots, no `onConnectionsChange`).

20. **Right-click context-menu + group facts (verified against the bundled LiteGraph `api-D9vMMk51.js`, frontend 1.43.18, May 2026 — these are recorded so agents do NOT re-grep the minified bundle, which costs ~30 min each time).** Reference implementation for ALL of this is `js/node_colors/index.js` (the Pixaroma Node/Group Colors menus).
    - **Three menu builders, three right-click targets, mutually exclusive.** `processContextMenu(node, event)` branches: a NODE under the cursor → `LGraphCanvas.prototype.getNodeMenuOptions(node)`; ELSE → `LGraphCanvas.prototype.getCanvasMenuOptions()` (the Add Node / Add Group / Paste menu), and THEN it appends an "Edit Group" entry when `graph.getGroupOnPos(event.canvasX, event.canvasY)` finds a group. So a node right-click NEVER reaches getCanvasMenuOptions — gating canvas-menu additions on "a group is under the cursor" can't double-add on nodes.
    - **Hook nodes via `getNodeMenuOptions`; hook canvas/groups via `getCanvasMenuOptions`.** Both are `LGraphCanvas.prototype` methods, both are wrapped by the Vue frontend via `registerWrapper`, and BOTH compose safely with a prototype monkey-patch (call original, then `options.push(null, ...entries)`) — proven by the node feature, coexists with rgthree. For TOP-LEVEL group entries (siblings of Add Node / Edit Group), patch `getCanvasMenuOptions`. The alternatives `LGraphGroup.prototype.getMenuOptions` (lands INSIDE the nested "Edit Group" submenu) and `LGraphCanvas.getGroupMenuOptions` (deprecated) are only for nested placement.
    - **`getCanvasMenuOptions()` takes NO arguments** — it cannot see the click event/position. To know WHICH group was right-clicked, read `this.graph_mouse` (graph-space `[x,y]`, the live cursor) and call `this.graph.getGroupOnPos(gm[0], gm[1])`. (`processContextMenu` uses `event.canvasX/canvasY`, but those aren't reachable from inside getCanvasMenuOptions.) Entries you push there render just ABOVE the "Edit Group" entry that processContextMenu appends afterward.
    - **`graph.getGroupOnPos(x, y)`** (graph coords) returns the `LGraphGroup` whose bounds contain the point, else `undefined`.
    - **Submenu callback signature is `function(value, options, mouseEvent, parentMenu, node)`.** A `has_submenu` item opens its child via `new LiteGraph.ContextMenu(items, { event: mouseEvent, parentMenu })`. Nesting works to ≥3 levels.
    - **Group data model:** a group has ONE color — `group.color` (any CSS string; default `#3f789e`, which is pale_blue's `groupcolor`). NO title/body split (nodes have `color` title + `bgcolor` body; groups don't). It serializes as `{id, title, bounding, color, flags}` into the workflow's top-level `groups[]` array and reloads natively, exactly like `node.color`. Recolor with `group.color = "#.."; group.setDirtyCanvas(false, true)` — no `recomputeInsideNodes()` needed for a color-only change.
    - **Group transparency is NOT adjustable per group.** `drawGroups` → `LGraphGroup.draw` hardcode the fill at `0.25 * editor_alpha` and the outline stroke at `1.0 * editor_alpha`. `editor_alpha` (default 1) is a GLOBAL canvas dimmer (also affects nodes + wires), not per-group. An `rgba()` in `group.color` only multiplies the alpha DOWN (max effective fill 0.25); you cannot make a single group MORE opaque without monkey-patching `LGraphGroup.draw`. We deliberately leave it native.
    - **Multi-select:** nodes via `canvas.selected_nodes` (plain object keyed by id); groups via `canvas.selectedItems` (a `Set` that mixes nodes AND groups — filter with `[...selectedItems].filter(x => x instanceof someGroup.constructor)`). There is NO `selected_groups` map.
    - **Node default colors:** `LiteGraph.NODE_DEFAULT_COLOR = "#333"`, `LiteGraph.NODE_DEFAULT_BGCOLOR = "#353535"`.
    - **Unregistered settings DO persist.** `app.ui.settings.setSettingValueAsync(id, val)` / `getSettingValue(id)` work for an id that is NOT in any extension's `settings[]` array — the backend saves `comfy.settings.json` as a plain JSON merge with NO allow-list, and `getSettingValue` returns the stored value (or `undefined` if unset). This is how `Pixaroma.NodeColors.Favorites` stores 4 favorite color pairs as one compact JSON blob with zero Settings-panel rows. Removing a setting's registration does NOT erase its stored value (one-time migrations can still read the old key).

### ComfyUI Nodes 2.0 Migration (LIVING SECTION — append what we learn)

ComfyUI is gradually making **Nodes 2.0** the default node renderer. It replaces LiteGraph's canvas painting of node bodies with **Vue/DOM components**. Today it is opt-in (Settings > Rendering, the `Comfy.VueNodes.Enabled` setting → flips `LiteGraph.vueNodesMode`), coexists with legacy mode, and is not forced. The plan: migrate Pixaroma node-by-node, testing each with the renderer toggled BOTH ways, and grow this section with every concrete fact we learn. Official migration docs were not released as of 2026-05, so the **reference implementations ARE the documentation**: ComfyUI core frontend (`Comfy-Org/ComfyUI_frontend`) and KJNodes (`kijai/ComfyUI-KJNodes`). Add new findings here as we hit them (per [[feedback_document_patterns_immediately]]).

> **STATUS: the migration is COMPLETE as of 2026-06-01** — every Pixaroma node AND every canvas feature (Align, Connection FX, Node Colors/Brand) works in both renderers. **GOING FORWARD, every NEW node/feature MUST be built for BOTH renderers from the start (never legacy-only) and tested with the Node UI toggled both ways before it's considered done.** Use the recipes in this section (DOM widgets → `applyAdaptiveCanvasOnly` + a `pixaroma_*` type; painted/fill UI → DOM overlays or bridged `addCustomWidget`, since `onDrawForeground` body paint is skipped in 2.0; branch on `isVueNodes()` for renderer-specific behavior). The per-node table + recipes below remain the reference.

**Diagnostic node: Version Check Pixaroma** (`nodes/node_version_check.py` + `js/version_check/index.js`, class `PixaromaVersionCheck`). On-canvas info panel with four rows — ComfyUI version (`/system_stats` → `system.comfyui_version`), Frontend version (`window.__COMFYUI_FRONTEND_VERSION__`), Node UI (`LiteGraph.vueNodesMode` → "Nodes 2.0" green / "Legacy" blue, polled every 600ms so it tracks a Settings toggle without reload — label is "Node UI" not "Renderer" because users don't know that word; the value is ALSO a one-click switch — clicking it flips `Comfy.VueNodes.Enabled` via `app.ui.settings.setSettingValueAsync` so users can swap renderers without opening Settings), and Pixaroma version (`GET /pixaroma/api/version`, a route that reads `pyproject.toml`). A Copy button copies all four lines as text for bug reports (computes the Node UI value from `vueNodesMode`, NOT the displayed text, so the ⇄ switch glyph isn't copied), and a Refresh button next to it clears Cache Storage + `location.reload()` (JS can't force a true HTTP-cache-bypass hard reload — Ctrl+Shift+R remains that; tooltip says so). Built with the recipe below (DOM widget + unique type `pixaroma_version_check` + `applyAdaptiveCanvasOnly`), so it doubles as a known-good reference for the pattern AND the fastest way to confirm which renderer a screenshot/session is in (don't infer renderer from pixels — read this panel or the Console). (Started life as "Renderer Check Pixaroma"; renamed + expanded before release.)

**The renderer toggle / how to branch in code.** The setting `Comfy.VueNodes.Enabled` drives `LiteGraph.vueNodesMode` (boolean, globally readable). For behavior that genuinely must differ between renderers, branch on it: `if (LiteGraph.vueNodesMode) { …vue path… } else { …canvas path… }` (KJNodes' `nodeswap.js` / `setgetnodes.js` pattern). Prefer approaches that need NO branch (see survival matrix).

**What survives vs breaks (verified from `ComfyUI_frontend` source, 2026-05).** In `vueNodesMode`, `LGraphCanvas.drawNode()` returns early after syncing slot metrics — so ALL node-body canvas painting is silently skipped (no warning). Widgets are re-dispatched by `useProcessedWidgets.ts`: `getComponent(widget.type) || (widget.isDOMWidget ? WidgetDOM : WidgetLegacy)`, gated first by `shouldRenderAsVue = !widget.options?.canvasOnly && !!widget.type`.

| Pattern | Legacy | Nodes 2.0 | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| `addDOMWidget(name,type,el)` | ✅ | ✅ | **Best dual-mode strategy.** `WidgetDOM.vue` re-parents your `el` into the Vue node body. Zero branching. |
| `addCustomWidget` w/ `draw()`+`mouse()` | ✅ | ✅ for FIXED-height controls; ❌ for fill/resize | Bridged by `WidgetLegacy.vue` — Vue-managed `<canvas>`, calls `widget.draw(ctx,node,w,y=1,h)` + `widget.mouse(e,[offsetX,offsetY],node)`. Caveats (see "Preview Image / painted-node Nodes 2.0 fill" below): (1) repaints ONLY via `widget.triggerDraw`, NOT `setDirtyCanvas`; (2) `y` passed is 1, `ctx.canvas` is its own canvas (graph_mouse hover + `node.size[1]-y` fill break); (3) the bridge's canvas+2 makes a flex/`auto` row grow 2px/pass → unbounded node growth. A bridged canvas can be a FIXED-height widget, but NEVER a fill-the-body widget — use a DOM widget for that. |
| `nodeType.prototype.onDrawForeground` (body paint) | ✅ | ❌ **silently skipped** | The big one. Painting controls directly on the node body (not via a widget) is NEVER bridged. No fallback. |
| `onDrawBackground` | ✅ | ❌ skipped | Same early-return. |
| `onMouseDown` hit-testing painted rects | ✅ | ⚠️ fires but rects are gone | Handler still runs, but there's nothing painted to hit-test against. |
| `widget.options.canvasOnly = true` | hidden from Parameters tab | ❌ **also excluded from the Vue body** | **TENSION — see below.** `shouldRenderAsVue` returns false → the widget renders NOWHERE in Nodes 2.0. |
| Monkey-patching `LGraphCanvas.prototype` (menus, `drawFrontCanvas`) | ✅ | ⚠️/❌ unreliable | Officially discouraged. Canvas-level overlays may still paint, but per-node painting won't. Right-click menu patches need per-case testing. |
| `node.color` / `node.bgcolor` | ✅ | ❓ verify | Likely maps to a Vue style but unconfirmed — test Brand + Node Colors early. |

**⚠️ The `canvasOnly` tension (affects MANY Pixaroma nodes) — RESOLVED, house rule below.** Vue Compat #15 told us to set `canvasOnly: true` on internal widgets to stop them duplicating into the right-sidebar Parameters tab. But in Nodes 2.0 that SAME flag (`shouldRenderAsVue = !options.canvasOnly`) excludes the widget from the node body entirely → it vanishes (verified empirically 2026-05 on Show Text: empty body in Nodes 2.0 while ComfyUI's own "Preview as Text" rendered fine).

**HOUSE RULE (settled on node #1 = Show Text):** make `canvasOnly` an ADAPTIVE LIVE getter — `true` in legacy, `false` in Nodes 2.0. In legacy the node body draws DOM widgets regardless of the flag, so `true` only hides it from the Parameters tab (still want that); in Nodes 2.0 `false` lets the Vue body render it. Use the shared helper: after `addDOMWidget`/`addCustomWidget`, call `applyAdaptiveCanvasOnly(widget)` (from `js/shared/nodes2.mjs`, re-exported by the shared barrel) and do NOT pass `canvasOnly` in the widget's own options literal. The helper defines `canvasOnly` as a getter on `widget.options` returning `!window.LiteGraph?.vueNodesMode`, evaluated fresh each render (also exports `isVueNodes()` for dual-branch code). Apply this to every node that currently sets `canvasOnly: true`: Preview Image (strip+buttons), Prompt Stack / Prompt Multi / Prompt Pack (rows), Switch family, Resolution, Note, Text, etc. — it's the standard first step of each node's migration.

**⚠️ Resizing a node in Nodes 2.0: a bare `node.size[1] = h` write can be REVERTED if the node was last sized in the OTHER renderer — use `node.setSize([w, h])` (verified on Prompt Stack, 2026-05).** Symptom: grow rows in legacy → switch to Nodes 2.0 → an action that should SHRINK the node (Prompt Stack Reset) leaves it tall; same-renderer add+shrink works fine. Probe showed the content measured correctly small (`getMinHeight() = 120`) but `node.size[1]` stuck at the old tall value (340) — the shrink's array-index assignment didn't persist. Nodes 2.0's reactive layout treats `node.size` as derived from a committed value and silently reverts a raw index mutation when the layout was committed under a different renderer; `node.setSize()` goes through LiteGraph's official resize path and sticks in both. Rule: any code that resizes a node programmatically (grow/fit/shrink helpers) should call `node.setSize?.([w, h])` (keep the direct `node.size[1] = h` as a fallback for builds without setSize). Mutating `node.size[0]`/`[1]` directly is still fine for the FRESH-default-size assignment in `onNodeCreated` (no prior committed layout to fight).

**⚠️ The Nodes 2.0 manual-resize MINIMUM height is a live measurement of the COLLAPSED node, NOT `getMinHeight` / `computeLayoutSize().minHeight` — so a DOM-widget body that can flex-collapse below its content overflows the frame when the user drags the node too small (verified by reading the frontend source, two agents, 2026-06; fixed on Find and Replace).** When you grab the resize handle, `useNodeResize.ts` does this at pointerdown: temporarily sets the node's `--node-height` CSS var to `0px`, reads `nodeElement.getBoundingClientRect().height`, and uses THAT as `minContentHeight`; the drag then clamps `newHeight >= minContentHeight`. It never consults `widget.getMinHeight` (that's only read by the DEFAULT `DOMWidget.computeLayoutSize` for `distributeSpace` math) nor `computeLayoutSize().minHeight` (the grid only uses the BOOLEAN `hasLayoutSize` to pick `'auto'` vs `'min-content'` for the row track — the returned minHeight NUMBER is discarded). So the ONLY thing that raises the drag floor is the DOM's own collapsed min-content height. Consequences:
- **Bug shape:** a widget root with `height:100%` + `min-height:0` (or a fill area with `flex:1 1 0; min-height:0`) collapses to ~0 under the `--node-height:0` measurement, so `minContentHeight` reads far below the real content → the user can drag the node small enough that fixed-height content (text rows) overflows below the frame. (Diagnostic on Find and Replace: `cell client H 173` while `computeLayoutSize.minHeight` was 264 and content `scrollHeight 244` → OVERFLOW.)
- **Why Compare / Preview Image / Save Mp4 DON'T have this:** their body is a single fit-contained `<canvas>`/`<img>`/`<video>` that scales to any size, so collapsing to ~0 just shrinks the image — nothing to overflow. Nodes with FIXED-height content (text rows: Find and Replace, Prompt Stack/Multi/Pack; the readout in Prompt Reader) need a real floor.
- **The FINAL working recipe (2026-06; legacy unaffected). This took ~15 wrong-turn commits across Find and Replace + Prompt Stack/Multi/Pack — apply ALL of it to any new DOM-widget node with fixed-height content (button rows / text rows), and watch BOTH axes:**
  1. **`node.size` min clamps in `onResize`/`onDrawForeground` MUST be gated `if (isVueNodes()) return` (LEGACY-ONLY). THE single biggest gotcha — it bit all four nodes.** In Nodes 2.0 the RENDERED node size lives in the Vue LAYOUT STORE, **not** `node.size`. If `onResize`/`onDrawForeground` clamp `node.size` to MIN_W/MIN_H, the Vue layer still renders the node at the dragged (smaller) size while `node.size` holds the clamped (bigger) value — a DESYNC. On a workflow switch the node is rebuilt from `node.size`, so it JUMPS to the clamped size. **User-visible tell: "make it SMALLER, switch workflow, it reverts to a BIGGER size; make it BIGGER and it keeps the size" — the asymmetry is diagnostic (only the smaller-than-min case trips the clamp).** Diagnostic trap that wasted hours: a logger reading `node.size` shows the SAME value before/after the switch while the rendered node visibly differs — **`node.size` LIES about the rendered size in Nodes 2.0; measure `element.getBoundingClientRect()` instead.** Every painted node already gated these clamps legacy-only; the four DOM nodes were missing it.
  2. **The squish FLOOR (so fixed content / button rows can't be dragged out of frame vertically) = the shared `js/shared/resize_floor.mjs::installResizeFloor(root, measureFn)`.** It pins `root.style.minHeight = measureFn(root)` ONLY WHILE A RESIZE HANDLE IS DRAGGED — armed on a CAPTURE-phase window `pointerdown` when the grabbed element's cursor is `*-resize` and the handle is in this node's `.lg-node`; cleared on pointerup/cancel. Because the min-height is present exactly when the frontend takes its `--node-height:0` collapse measurement, the drag clamps at the content floor; because it's gone the rest of the time, it NEVER inflates `node.size` on a load/switch (no jump). Wire `node._pixXxFloorOff = installResizeFloor(root, measure)` after `addDOMWidget`, uninstall in `onRemoved`. `measureRootContent(root)` (same module) is the generic flex-column measure for a node with no measure of its own (Prompt Pack). **This is the CORRECT JS floor — DISTINCT from the abandoned always-on / load-path variant (below).**
  3. **Action BUTTON rows need `flex-wrap: wrap` (HORIZONTAL spill — a SEPARATE axis from the vertical floor).** The Nodes 2.0 node body is NARROWER than legacy, so a 3-4 button row sized for legacy doesn't fit and the last button (Reset/Clear) spills out the RIGHT edge. Add `flex-wrap:wrap` to the action container so buttons wrap to a second line (the floor grows the node to fit). A NESTED button container (Prompt Pack's `.pix-pp-actions` inside `.pix-pp-bottombar`) ALSO needs `flex:0 1 auto; min-width:0` or it stays content-sized and never wraps. **The vertical floor (#2) does NOT fix horizontal spill — check both axes when a user reports "buttons outside the node".**
  4. **The DEFAULT-size write in `onNodeCreated` must be FRESH-ONLY** — either assign `node.size` SYNCHRONOUSLY before `configure()` overwrites it (Prompt Multi/Pack), OR gate the microtask write on a `_pixXxConfigured` flag set in `onConfigure` (Find and Replace, Prompt Stack). A microtask `if (size < DEFAULT) size = DEFAULT` that runs AFTER configure reverts a user-shrunk-below-DEFAULT node to DEFAULT on every switch.
  5. **A LIVE `getMinHeight` measurement must be COARSE-ROUNDED** (`Math.round(h/4)*4`) or font/sub-pixel jitter creeps `node.size` bigger every switch (grow-to-content is grow-only); a CONSTANT (Prompt Pack `WIDGET_MIN_H`, Text Overlay `BASE_H`) is even better.
  6. **CSS still matters but is NOT sufficient alone:** the root must NOT have `height:100%` (it collapses to 0 under the `--node-height:0` measurement); give the flex/fill area a real `min-height`. BUT the host wraps the root in `*:flex-1`, so the root can still flex-shrink below content — CSS alone does NOT guarantee the floor; the during-resize `installResizeFloor` (#2) is what guarantees it. (An earlier note here claimed "CSS-only, do NOT reach for JS" — that was WRONG; `installResizeFloor` is the needed JS.)
  7. **Auto-grow textareas: pin EMPTY fields to one line** (`if (!ta.value) { ta.style.height='30px'; return }`) — else when the node is narrow the empty field's wrapped PLACEHOLDER balloons `scrollHeight` and the field grows tall and won't shrink back (autoGrow only runs on input). Re-measure all fields on a WIDTH-change `ResizeObserver` so a field that wrapped at a narrow width shrinks when the node is widened.
- **⚠️ ABANDONED — the ALWAYS-ON / LOAD-PATH JS floor (DISTINCT from `installResizeFloor` above; do NOT confuse them).** Find and Replace first tried `applyRootMinHeight` (set `root.style.minHeight = measure()` on EVERY content change INCLUDING `onConfigure`) + a `ResizeObserver` that called `node.setSize` whenever the rendered height dropped below content. Both backfired and were removed: (a) writing a content-derived size on the LOAD path makes grow-to-content inflate `node.size` → jump-on-switch + false-dirty; (b) the `ResizeObserver`'s `setSize` fires DURING a drag and desyncs the **Align** resize-guard → Align moves the SELECTED node. The WORKING version is `installResizeFloor` (during-resize ONLY, NO `setSize`). **Rules: never write a content-derived size on the load path; never `setSize` from a `ResizeObserver` that can fire mid-drag.**
- **A LIVE `getMinHeight`/`computeLayoutSize` measurement must be COARSE-ROUNDED** (e.g. `Math.round(h/4)*4`) or sub-pixel/font jitter creeps `node.size` bigger on every workflow switch (grow-to-content is grow-only and accumulates). Prompt Stack / Multi / Find-and-Replace round to a 4px grid; a CONSTANT (Prompt Pack `WIDGET_MIN_H`, Text Overlay `BASE_H`) is even better — byte-identical every load, never creeps.
- **Dead ends (do NOT waste time on):** returning a bigger `minHeight` from a custom `computeLayoutSize` (discarded for grid row sizing); setting `widget.options.getMinHeight`/`getMaxHeight` (only feeds `distributeSpace`, not the resize floor); `constructor.min_height` (canvas/legacy `computeSize` path only). The resize floor reads the DOM, full stop — the fix must live in CSS/DOM (make the content un-collapsible to its true floor). `computeLayoutSize` IS still worth defining (its existence makes the widget an `'auto'` grower row so a fill area can expand), just don't rely on its returned minHeight as a floor; keep `minWidth: 1` so the saved node width round-trips (Compare gotcha 2).

**⚠️ A hidden internal STRING widget (`hideJsonWidget`) shows its raw JSON at the TOP of the node in Nodes 2.0 unless `canvasOnly` is set (fixed at the helper, 2026-05).** Nodes that keep a serialized-state STRING widget + hide it with `js/shared/utils.mjs::hideJsonWidget` (Note's `note_json`, and label / image_resize / load_image / resolution) were only hiding it via `hidden=true` + `computeSize=[0,-4]` + `display:none` — which works in legacy but NOT in Nodes 2.0, where the widget's `STRING`/`customtext` type still renders it as a textarea showing the raw `{"version":1,...}` JSON above the node's real UI. Fix: `hideJsonWidget` now also sets `w.options.canvasOnly = true` (static — this widget must stay hidden in BOTH renderers), so `shouldRenderAsVue = !canvasOnly` excludes it from the Vue body AND it stays out of the legacy Parameters tab. One helper edit fixed every consumer.

**⚠️ DOM-widget TYPE must not collide with a registered Vue widget type (verified on Show Text, 2026-05).** `addDOMWidget(name, TYPE, el, opts)` — if `TYPE` is one of the names in `widgetRegistry.ts` (`customtext`, `textarea`, `multiline`, `string`, `text`, `number`, `slider`, `toggle`, `combo`, `color`, `markdown`, `button`, …), Nodes 2.0's dispatch `getComponent(widget.type) || (isDOMWidget ? WidgetDOM : WidgetLegacy)` matches the FIRST branch and renders ITS OWN native Vue widget — your custom DOM element is created but never mounted (orphaned, `isConnected === false`), so anything you write to it (e.g. `onExecuted` setting the textarea value) lands on a detached element and the on-screen box stays empty. Symptom: box renders but is blank; console probe shows `widget value: "1.1"` while `textarea still in page?: false`. Fix: give the DOM widget a UNIQUE, namespaced type string (Show Text now uses `"pixaroma_showtext"`) so `getComponent` returns undefined and it falls through to `WidgetDOM.vue`, which re-parents YOUR element. The type is cosmetic in the legacy renderer (DOM widgets render regardless of type there) and does NOT affect serialization (that keys off the widget NAME + `serialize`), so renaming is safe both ways. **House rule: Pixaroma DOM widgets use a `pixaroma_*` type name.** Audit other nodes for registered-type collisions when migrating each.

**⚠️ `image_upload: True` nodes get a Nodes 2.0 native `.image-preview` panel that `node.imgs` suppression does NOT reach (verified on Prompt Reader, 2026-05).** Locking `node.imgs` to `[]` (Preview Image Pattern #15) kills the LEGACY bottom-of-node preview AND the `$$canvas-image-preview` widget, but Nodes 2.0 ALSO renders its own `div.image-preview` inside `div.lg-node-content` (part of the Vue `LGraphNode` component), fed by ComfyUI's internal node-preview state — NOT `node.imgs`. So it shows regardless of the suppression, and it goes STALE on programmatic file changes (our custom dropdown sets `widget.value` without firing the native image-upload refresh, Pattern #3), displaying a previously-loaded image. The DOM chain that identifies it: `img.object-contain < div.image-preview < div.lg-node-content < div.lg-node`. Fix (when you want NO preview): one CSS rule scoped to the node via `:has()` — `.lg-node:has(.<your-root-class>) .image-preview { display: none !important; }` (Prompt Reader uses `.pix-pr-root`). No JS/observer needed; legacy has no `.lg-node`/`.image-preview` so it's a no-op there. If a node WANTS a correct preview instead, hide the native one the same way and render your own `<img>` in the DOM widget, refreshed on every file change. **This will matter for the Load Image migration too** (also `image_upload: True`).

**✅ Fullscreen editors render + work under Nodes 2.0 (confirmed on Text Overlay, 2026-05).** A fullscreen editor is its own DOM/WebGL overlay appended to `document.body` (not part of the node body), so it is renderer-agnostic — Text Overlay's editor opened, dragged text on canvas, and Save/Save-to-Disk/Undo/Redo/Close all worked in Nodes 2.0. This strongly implies Paint / 3D / Composer / Crop / AudioReact / Note editors are also fine in Nodes 2.0; only their NODE-BODY surface (launch button + DOM preview widget) needs the canvasOnly recipe, and the "Open …" button must live inside the DOM widget (as Text Overlay's does) so it renders in the Vue body. Still verify each, but expect quick wins.

**The genuinely hard case: per-slot UI aligned with input dots.** Switch / Mute Switch / Switch Source paint toggles + labels on the SAME row as each input dot via `onDrawForeground` + slot-Y math (Vue Compat #16). In Nodes 2.0 the slots are Vue-rendered and there is no canvas to align to. These need a real rethink (DOM widget per row), not a mechanical port.

**VERIFIED (2026-05-29, reading the live `ComfyUI_frontend` source, not the legacy notes): in Nodes 2.0 you CANNOT put any control on an input row. `src/renderer/extensions/vueNodes/components/InputSlot.vue` renders EXACTLY two things - a `SlotConnectionDot` + a text label `span` (`slotData.label || localized_name || ...`). There is no slot/markup for a widget on the input row.** `NodeSlots.vue` is a two-column flex (`flex justify-between`): inputs in a left `flex-col`, outputs in a right `flex-col`, each slot one row of dot+label. Widgets render SEPARATELY in `NodeWidgets.vue` BELOW the slots block (per `NodeContent`'s `flex-col`: header → slots → content → widgets → footer). The newer "Widget Input Socket model" (RFC #9) `linkedWidgetInputs` is only bookkeeping for which inputs co-exist with a body widget - it still renders the widget in the body, NOT on the input row. So a per-input toggle MUST live in a body DOM widget below the dots; aligning it to the dot row is impossible in the current renderer (true for EVERY node, core included - that's why core dynamic-input nodes also stack controls below). Do NOT spend time trying to align; do NOT re-grep the frontend for this.

**Vue dot labels can be set, but ONLY refresh on (re)load - a live `slot.label` mutation does NOT update the dot (VERIFIED 2026-05-29).** `GraphNodeManager.extractVueNodeData` builds a `shallowReactive` COPY of the node's inputs/outputs/widgets; the dot label is `slotData.label` on that copy. `shallowReactive` does NOT track a nested mutation like `node.inputs[i].label = x`, and there is no public hook to notify the sync layer (it listens to internal `LGraphNodeProperties` events). The connection DOT fill updates live (links go through a separate reactive path), but the LABEL text does not - it only re-reads when the node re-mounts (workflow open / Ctrl+F5). Consequences for a dynamic-input node:
  - A type-based dot label ("string 1") goes STALE after a rewire (the user sees "string 2" on a dot now carrying IMAGE) - bad. A custom-name dot label goes stale after a rename. Neither updates until reload.
  - **Decision (Switch, 2026-05-29): give Vue dots a STABLE, index-only label = `input N`** (set via `slotDisplayLabel`, branched: `"​"` zero-width in legacy so the canvas paint isn't double-drawn, `input ${N}` in Nodes 2.0). It never depends on type or custom name, so it never goes stale and never needs a live refresh. The live, volatile detail (wire type + custom name) lives in the body DOM list (which IS our own DOM and re-renders on demand). `slot.label` is serialized, so this is diff-gated (write only when different) → same-renderer reloads stay clean; opening a workflow ACROSS renderers ("​" ↔ "input N") flags it modified once (acceptable, documented precedent). Do NOT try to feed type/name onto the Vue dot - it can't refresh live; put it in the body list.

**Switch family Nodes 2.0 pattern (established on Switch, 2026-05-29):** per-renderer split via `if (isVueNodes())` in `onNodeCreated`. Legacy keeps the canvas paint (`onDrawForeground`) + hit-test (`onMouseDown`) UNCHANGED, each gated to early-return when `isVueNodes()`. Nodes 2.0 builds ONE DOM list widget (`js/switch/vue_list.mjs`) - one row per input, in dot ORDER, below the dots: `[input N (fixed, matches the dot)] [editable field: placeholder = the wire type "string"/"image", value = a custom name that REPLACES the type once typed] [mutex toggle]`. No separate type tag - the editable field IS where the type shows (as its placeholder) and where you rename (user pick, 2026-05-29). The Vue input DOTS themselves show the same stable `input N` (per the dot-label note above - type/name can't live-refresh on a dot, so the live type lives here in the list field, which DOES re-render). The field writes the SAME `state.labels` the legacy paint reads (so a rename shows in both renderers); clicking the row activates it, clicking the field edits it. Shared mutator `setActiveRow()` lives in core.mjs and is called by BOTH the legacy `onMouseDown` and the Vue row click. Core calls `node._pixSwRefresh?.()` (the list's render fn, set only in Vue; no-op in legacy) after every slot/state change so the list re-renders on connect/disconnect/activate. The list widget uses `applyAdaptiveCanvasOnly`, a namespaced type (`pixaroma_switch_list`), and a getMinHeight==getMaxHeight = rows*26+8. Mute Switch will reuse this exact shape + a top mode-pill bar (DOM segmented toggles, like Prompt Pack). Renaming-on-the-dot and toggle-on-the-dot-row are both impossible per the VERIFIED note above; the body list is the answer.

**Migration playbook (default approach per node):**
1. Toggle Nodes 2.0 ON, observe the node, note exactly what's missing/broken (screenshot).
2. If the node already uses `addDOMWidget` → likely fine; just resolve the `canvasOnly` flag.
3. If it paints via `onDrawForeground` body painting → move that UI into either a proper `addCustomWidget` with `draw()`+`mouse()` (bridged for free) OR a DOM widget with its own render loop (`requestAnimationFrame`/`ResizeObserver`, since `onDrawForeground`'s polling tick is gone).
4. If it's a canvas-wide patch (Align guides, Connection FX) → branch on `vueNodesMode` or accept it only runs in legacy.
5. Verify with the toggle BOTH ways; saved-workflow load must stay clean (Vue Compat #18 still applies).
6. Record the concrete pattern + gotchas back here.

**`getCustomWidgets()` extension hook** — official way to register a custom widget TYPE: return `{ MY_TYPE: (node,inputName,inputData,app) => node.addDOMWidget(inputName,"MY_TYPE",el) }`. The result is a DOM widget → goes through `WidgetDOM.vue`. Useful if we ever want a Python-declared input to mount a Pixaroma DOM widget.

### Preview Image / painted-node Nodes 2.0 fill — the hard-won recipe (READ before migrating Load Image, Compare, Reference, or any node with a fill-the-body preview)

Preview Image was the first "painted" node migrated and it took many rounds. Every fact below is verified empirically against frontend 1.43.18 (ComfyUI 0.22.3) and the bundle. The headline: **a bridged-canvas custom widget CANNOT fill-and-resize in Nodes 2.0 — you must use a DOM widget for any preview that should grow with the node.** Reference impl: `js/preview/index.js`.

1. **`addCustomWidget` with `draw()`+`mouse()` IS bridged in Nodes 2.0 (WidgetLegacy), BUT the bridge has three traps that break a "fill the body" widget:**
   - **The bridge repaints ONLY via `widget.triggerDraw`, NOT on `node.setDirtyCanvas`.** So async updates (image finished loading, a toast, a selection change) leave the canvas frozen on its first paint. You must call `widget.triggerDraw?.()` (it's assigned by the bridge on mount). Symptom if missed: "preview shows nothing" / "Save button does nothing, no toast" even though the action ran. Our `repaint(node)` helper pokes triggerDraw for canvas widgets (and the DOM render fn for DOM widgets).
   - **`draw(ctx, node, width, y, h)` — the bridge passes `y=1` (NOT node-relative) and a 5th `height` arg = the widget's canvas height; `ctx.canvas` is the bridge's own `<canvas>`, not the main LiteGraph canvas.** So the legacy "fill the rest of the body via `node.size[1] - y`" trick computes a huge wrong height. And `app.canvas.graph_mouse` hover math (node-relative) doesn't map to the widget canvas → canvas-painted hover silently stops working in Nodes 2.0 (clicks still work via `widget.mouse(e,[offsetX,offsetY],node)` which uses canvas-local coords that DO match your draw rects).
   - **The bridge sizes the canvas to `(computedHeight+2)*dpr`. If you make the widget a flex/`auto` row (see #3), that +2 makes the `auto` grid cell grow 2px every layout pass → UNBOUNDED node growth on every run AND resize.** This is THE growth bug. A bridged canvas can be a FIXED-height widget safely, but it can never flex-fill.

2. **Native PreviewImage doesn't hit any of this because it is a DOM Vue component (`flex-auto`), not a bridged canvas.** That's the model to copy for fill.

3. **The node body in Nodes 2.0 is a CSS GRID. Each widget is one row. A widget WITH a `computeLayoutSize` method → flexible `auto` row (can grow); WITHOUT → fixed `min-content` row.** (Bundle: `widgets.map(w => shouldExpand(w.type)||w.hasLayoutSize ? 'auto' : 'min-content')`, `hasLayoutSize = typeof w.computeLayoutSize === 'function'`.) Consequences:
   - To make a preview FILL, give it `computeLayoutSize` (→ `auto` row) so it absorbs the node's free vertical space.
   - **CRITICAL: only ONE widget may be an `auto` row, or the grid splits the free space between them.** `addDOMWidget` assigns a DEFAULT `computeLayoutSize`, so a sibling DOM widget (e.g. our buttons row) silently becomes a competing `auto` row → the preview only gets HALF the slack and never fills (symptom: image small, big gap above it). FIX: on the fixed sibling widget set `widget.computeLayoutSize = undefined` (delete it) so it's a `min-content` (content-height) row, leaving the preview as the sole grower. Pinning it with `min===max` computeLayoutSize does NOT work — the CSS grid still sees it as `auto` and gives it space (the LiteGraph maxHeight is ignored by the CSS grid).
   - `node.size` does NOT drive the Nodes 2.0 node-body height the way `computedHeight` (LiteGraph's distributeSpace) suggests — the two disagree. Trust the CSS grid (`computeLayoutSize` + the flex fill below), NOT `node.size`-derived computeSize (that loops/grows).

4. **A DOM widget's element only FILLS its allocated row if you defeat the flex `min-height:auto` default.** ComfyUI wraps your `addDOMWidget` element in a host `<div class="flex flex-col *:flex-1">` (a flex column whose children get `flex:1`). A flex item defaults to `min-height:auto` (= its content height), so it collapses to content (e.g. 526px) instead of filling the allocated height (887px). Your element MUST have `flex:1 1 0; min-height:0;` (drop any `height:100%`/`min-height:Npx` — they fight it; the floor is guaranteed by `computeLayoutSize.minHeight`). Mirror native ImagePreview: container `flex-auto min-h-0`, image `position:absolute; inset:0; width:100%; height:100%; object-fit:contain`. Then size your inner canvas to `root.clientWidth/Height` via a `ResizeObserver` and draw — no canvas-bridge +2, so no growth.

5. **The DOM strip REUSES the canvas widget's `draw()`/`mouse()` unchanged** by instantiating a throwaway `createStripWidget()` and calling `logic.draw(ctx, node, cssW, 0, cssH)` from the ResizeObserver render; clicks come from a DOM `pointerdown` on the root (container-local coords share the `y=0` origin the render draws with, so they hit-test `node._pixaromaCells` directly). This keeps legacy and Nodes 2.0 pixel-identical from ONE draw implementation.

6. **Per-renderer widget choice is decided ONCE in `onNodeCreated` via `if (isVueNodes())`** (legacy → `addCustomWidget` canvas; Nodes 2.0 → `addDOMWidget` DOM). The renderer is fixed per page load, so only one path is live per node instance. **Switching the renderer live (Version Check toggle) leaves existing nodes built for the old renderer → they misbehave until a page refresh.** This is expected/unavoidable with the per-renderer-widget approach; tell the user to Ctrl+F5 after toggling. (Optional QoL: make the Version Check toggle auto-reload.)

7. **`node.hideOutputImages = true` is the OFFICIAL way to suppress ComfyUI's native output-image preview** (set it in onNodeCreated). Needed because emitting `ui.images` (for the Media Assets panel refresh, Preview Pattern #14) makes the Vue node render its OWN `.image-preview` panel — a duplicate that also compounds node height each run. The Vue preview-media computed early-returns when `hideOutputImages` is truthy (verified in GraphView bundle: `if (!images.length || node.hideOutputImages) return`), while `ui.images` still fires for Assets. Far cleaner than the marker-class + CSS `.image-preview{display:none}` hack (which flashed and got stripped on Vue re-render).

8. **Canvas-painted button row clips/overlaps in Nodes 2.0** (the bridge gives a canvas widget less usable width than legacy for the same node width). Two fixes used: (a) for the LEGACY canvas buttons, a SOFT floor in `computeButtonRects` (`Math.max(28, …)` instead of `Math.max(BTN_MIN_W, …)`) so the row shrinks to fit instead of overflowing the frame; (b) for NODES 2.0, render the buttons as a real DOM `<button>` flex row (`flex:1 1 0; min-width:0; text-overflow:ellipsis`) — fits any width, never overlaps, AND restores hover for free. Toasts become a DOM banner overlay; `repaint()` refreshes the buttons' `disabled` state.

**Net takeaway for the remaining painted nodes:** if the node just needs FIXED-height painted controls, a bridged `addCustomWidget` + `triggerDraw` repaints + adaptive canvasOnly is enough. If it needs a preview/area that FILLS and resizes, go DOM: one `auto`-row DOM widget with `flex:1 1 0; min-height:0`, every sibling widget as `min-content` (`computeLayoutSize = undefined`), `ResizeObserver`-sized inner canvas, and reuse the legacy `draw()` for identical rendering.

**⚠️ A DOM `<canvas>` widget MUST size its backing store at `dpr × graph-zoom`, NOT just `dpr` — otherwise it goes blurry/pixelated when the user zooms IN (issue #60, fixed 2026-06).** The Nodes 2.0 node body is CSS-transform-scaled by the graph zoom (`app.canvas.ds.scale`). A `<canvas>` has a FIXED backing store, so sizing it only at `clientWidth * devicePixelRatio` (layout px) means the browser CSS-stretches that fixed bitmap up by the zoom factor → soft/pixelated (native ComfyUI dodges this entirely by previewing through a resolution-independent `<img>`, which is why `shared/preview.mjs` mini-previews + Pause Image + Save Mp4's `<video>` are all immune — only canvas-rendered node-body content is affected). Two compounding facts: (a) the backing store must be `dpr * max(1, zoom)` (capped on the long side so a deep zoom can't allocate a giant canvas); (b) a `ResizeObserver` does NOT fire on graph zoom (the element's `clientWidth` in layout px is unchanged — only the CSS transform scale changes), so the canvas never re-renders at the new resolution on its own. Both are solved by the SHARED helpers in `js/shared/nodes2.mjs`: `canvasBackingScale(cssW, cssH)` (use in place of the bare `dpr` in every `canvas.width = …` + `ctx.setTransform(…)` pair) and `installZoomRepaint(node, () => [cssW, cssH], render, "_xxxZoomRaf")` (a per-frame rAF loop that repaints only when the scale changes; cancel it in `onRemoved` via `cancelAnimationFrame(node._xxxZoomRaf)`). Compare was the original reference implementation (inline); the helpers are that code promoted to shared. EVERY new node-body DOM canvas MUST use them.
