Output/input order matches the suite: Crop outputs `image, mask, crop_info, width, height`; Stitch inputs `image, mask, crop_info`; Stitch outputs `image, original` (the full uncropped original, straight from `crop_info["image"]`, so before/after compare with Image Compare is two short wires from the END of the chain - NOT on the Crop node).

2. **The geometry (`compute_region`) is mirrored JS↔Python and MUST stay in lockstep.** `nodes/_inpaint_helpers.py::compute_region` (Python authoritative, runs at execute) and `js/inpaint_crop/geometry.mjs::computeRegion` (editor's live crop-rectangle preview). bbox → context expand (`context_px` + `context_pct`) → size mode (keep/force/free, multiple-of-8, min/max guards, allow_upscale) → clamp to image. Only accepted drift: sub-pixel rect placement (Python banker's rounding vs JS round-half-up = ±1px preview). The throwaway harness `D:\Claude Tests\_inpaint_test.py` asserts the round-trip + geometry + seam math; re-run it (with the embedded python) after ANY helper change.

3. **THE SEAM is an OUTWARD-only feather (`_blur_alpha`) - do NOT make it centred/inward.** `blend_mode=mask` composites the inpainted crop back using a feathered mask: alpha = 1.0 everywhere INSIDE the mask AND at its edge, ramping to 0 over `blend` px OUTSIDE (scipy `distance_transform_edt` signed distance → `t = clip(signed/k + 1, 0, 1)` → smoothstep; no-scipy fallback = gaussian-blur the binary then `np.where(mask, 1.0, blurred)`). This is the whole point: a CENTRED feather made the masked content semi-transparent at its OWN edge → the old content ghosted through (the user's "visible halo at any blend"). Earlier wrong attempts (do NOT revert to): (a) `_feather_alpha` (distance-to-RECTANGLE-edge) on the mask - barely touches a mask whose edge is inside the crop, so the slider did nothing; (b) dilate-then-gaussian - pushed a FULL-STRENGTH halo outward so BIGGER blend looked WORSE. `_feather_alpha` (rectangle fade) is still correct for `blend_mode=whole_crop` only. Coverage is the crop node's `mask_grow`; the stitch only softens. **v3 (Option B): the feather has NO rect-edge guard and NO core-opaque clamp - instead `compute_region` grows the crop context to `max(context_px, blend)` (Pattern 5 + `docs/inpaint-crop-math.md` §1) so the mask always sits >= blend px from the crop edge and the outward smoothstep reaches 0 before the border on its own (opaque inside by construction). The v2 guard (`min(feather, smoothstep(de/k))` + a `max(.., mask)` core clamp) was REMOVED - it crushed a too-wide feather and could ghost a mask sitting near the crop edge. Trade-off: a big softness makes the crop a bit larger (the crop box grows in the editor). The editor seam-tint PREVIEW (`render.mjs::_seamAlphaCanvas`) now mirrors the scipy smoothstep too - a downscaled chamfer-DT via `geometry.mjs::seamAlphaFromAlpha` - so preview == result. See `docs/inpaint-crop-math.md` §3/§4.**

4. **Mask resizes ALWAYS use NEAREST, never bilinear** (apply_inpaint_crop out-mask + stitch_back alpha). Bilinear adds its OWN gradient halo on top of the feather (a SECOND softening). The brush is CRISP (the Soft-edge slider was removed in v2; `softness=0`), so `softm = np.maximum(raw, proc)` is just the filled+grown binary core; conditioning softness comes only from `mask_blur`. The conditioning out-mask gets the deliberate `mask_blur` gaussian; the stitch seam gets the deliberate `blend` feather - one intentional softening each, never two.

5. **Seam settings are SPLIT three ways (v2 + user feedback): `softness` = Crop node widget (mirrored in the editor), `blend_mode` = editor-only state, `color_match` = Stitch node widget.** `softness` (0-150, the seam feather = stitch `blend`) is a native Crop INT widget AND the editor's Softness slider, mirrored like the geometry knobs (`node_inpaint_crop.py::run` feeds it into the crop geometry as `params["blend"]` so the crop CONTEXT grows to fit the feather - `compute_region` uses `max(context_px, blend)`, Option B / Pattern 3 - AND injects it into `crop_info["blend"]`; the editor's `writeBackWidgets` writes the slider back to the `softness` widget on Save; `readParams` reads it). `blend_mode` (mask/whole_crop) is editor-only `state_json` -> `crop_info["blend_mode"]`. `color_match` (off/subtle/strong) is the Inpaint STITCH node's OWN widget - a post-result tweak with no live preview (it was briefly in the editor in early v2, moved back per user feedback); it is NOT in `crop_info`. The crop knobs (`size_mode/target/multiple/context_px/mask_grow/mask_blur/softness`) are all native Crop widgets AND mirrored into the editor; on Save the editor writes ALL back via `writeBackWidgets`. The Stitch node reads `blend`+`blend_mode` from `crop_info` (defaults `16`/`mask` when absent - e.g. an Image Crop `crop_info`) and `color_match` from its own widget. The brush `Soft edge` slider was removed - the brush is crisp; the editor's `Softness` slider owns seam softness with a live (approximate) DPR-backed preview tinted in a switchable color (`Pixaroma.Inpaint.PreviewColor` setting, display-only). `color_match` matches the inpaint over the UNMASKED CONTEXT (surroundings outside the mask), NOT the mask or the whole crop (both include the masked area and drag a deliberately-changed color back - red->white dress goes pink); it corrects only lighting/tone drift in the unchanged surroundings (falls back to uniform if the mask fills the crop). It is for blending an inpaint INTO the scene, not for deliberate recolors. Seam preview math now mirrors `_blur_alpha`'s SCIPY smoothstep (`render.mjs::_seamAlphaCanvas` via `geometry.mjs::seamAlphaFromAlpha`, a downscaled `(1,√2)` chamfer DT) so preview == result; see `docs/inpaint-crop-math.md` §4.

6. **Editor brush: per-stroke buffer + `lighten` composite + blur-on-bake.** Stamps are crisp white discs drawn on `_sctx` (the per-stroke buffer) with `globalCompositeOperation="lighten"` (max-blend → overlapping stamps can't stack into a hard/dark rim regardless of stroke speed); at stroke end `_compositeStroke` bakes the buffer onto the mask with a gaussian of width `softness*radius`. **v2: the Soft-edge slider was removed and `softness` is fixed at 0, so blur-on-bake is off and the brush is CRISP** (the stamps' anti-aliased discs still prevent jaggies); seam softness is the `Softness`/`blend` slider instead. The mask canvas is white-RGB + per-pixel-alpha (export composites over black → grayscale; the brush soft edge survives). `_exportMaskDataURL` uses `_effectiveMaskCanvas()` so a Ctrl+S mid-drag saves the in-progress stroke; undo/redo mid-drag call `_abandonStroke()` so the abandoned stroke isn't re-baked on mouseup.

7. **Split the mask bbox SCAN from the region COMPUTE.** `_rescanBBox()` (expensive full-image `getImageData` + per-pixel scan) runs ONLY on a mask change (stroke end / clear / invert / undo / redo / mask-load / image-load); `_recomputeRegion()` reads the cached `this._bbox` and is cheap, so the context-margin slider can re-preview on every tick without re-scanning. Every mask-mutation path must call `_rescanBBox()` before `_recomputeRegion()`.

8. **The painting canvas is DPR-backed** (`_fitCanvas`: `canvas.width = dispW*dpr`, `canvas.style.width = dispW px`, `ctx.setTransform(dpr,...)`; draw in LOGICAL px via `this._dispW`/`this._dispH`, init 0 in the constructor, set by `_fitCanvas`). The red tint overlay canvas is ALSO DPR-backed (backing `W*dpr`, drawn back at logical `W`) or it's blurry on HiDPI. **`clearRect` RESPECTS the canvas transform** (per the HTML spec - a common misconception says it doesn't), so clearing with logical dims under `setTransform(dpr)` clears the full canvas correctly; do NOT "fix" it to multiply by dpr (the 3-round review raised this as a false positive twice). `_displayPos` returns CSS px from `getBoundingClientRect`; `_scale = dispW/imgW`; pointer + brush + cursor math all stay in logical px - no DPR in the coordinate math.

9. **Dirty-on-load + persistence:** `node.size` is gated on `!isGraphLoading()`; `onConnectionsChange` gated on `isGraphLoading()`; the `InpaintCropWidget` DOM widget carries `{state_json}` (src_path + mask_path + doc dims) accepted via the FlexibleOptionalInputType (same mechanism as Image Crop's CropWidget); `IS_CHANGED` uses `json.dumps(sort_keys=True)` (key-order deterministic) + tracks mask_path AND src_path mtime. Device: crop outputs `.to(image.device)`; stitch pairs `image`+`original` to the same batch (trim BOTH to `min(B,C)`) and device.

10. **The 3-round review lesson:** human-review the agent findings, don't auto-apply. The review (correctly) caught the bilinear halo, the ghosting feather, and the batch-pairing crash; it ALSO raised false positives that needed rejecting (the `clearRect`-ignores-transform misconception; "canvas listener leaks" that are actually GC'd with the fresh-per-open overlay). Default to outward feather, NEAREST mask resize, and one intentional softening per stage.

11. **Mask source precedence: a PAINTED editor mask wins, but an empty/cleared one falls back to the wired `mask` input - via `resolve_inpaint_mask` in `_inpaint_helpers.py`.** The crop node has TWO mask sources - the wired `mask` input and the mask painted in its own editor (saved to `mask_path` in `state_json`). Clearing the editor (or saving without painting) writes an ALL-BLACK mask file while `mask_path` STAYS SET, so the old "disk mask wins whenever it loads (not None)" let that empty file silently override the wired mask -> `apply_inpaint_crop` saw no painted pixels -> `mask_bbox` None -> it cropped the WHOLE image (user report 2026-06-16: "I painted, then cleared the editor and ran, and it stopped using my wired mask"). `run()` now routes both through `resolve_inpaint_mask(disk_mask, upstream_mask)`: the disk mask wins ONLY when it has painted pixels (`max > 1e-6`); empty or absent -> the wired mask is used; neither -> None (whole image). Unit-tested in the harness (`test_cleared_editor_mask_falls_back_to_wired` + `test_painted_editor_mask_wins` + `test_no_editor_mask_uses_wired` + `test_no_masks_returns_none`). **KNOWN GAP (follow-up "Part B", not yet built):** the editor does NOT import the wired mask, so you can't see/paint ON TOP of it - opening the editor starts blank. The `mask` input tooltip was corrected to match the actual Part A behavior (it no longer claims "loads into the editor"); if Part B lands, have Python save the wired mask to temp for the editor to load (mirror `_save_source_temp` + the `pixaroma_inpaint_source` ui-payload flow) and restore the "paint on top" wording.

> **⚠️ WIP HANDOFF v2 — Inpaint editor rework (rewritten 2026-06-16; DELETE once the softness rework lands + released).**
> **STATE:** the Inpaint pair + its "editor v2" is BUILT and committed on **`Ioan`** (latest CLEAN commit **`7a85572`**); torch harness green. v2 (this session) changed: `softness` is a Crop-node INT widget 0-150 → `crop_info["blend"]`, mirrored in the editor; `color_match` is the STITCH node's own knob and matches the UNMASKED CONTEXT (`a<0.5`), not the mask/whole-crop (so a deliberate recolor isn't dragged back); `_blur_alpha` = outward smoothstep feather (the rect-edge guard + `max(..,mb)` core clamp were REMOVED in softness rework Part 1 - the crop now grows to fit the feather instead); `_dilate` = fast scipy `maximum_filter`/numpy separable (was ~50s PIL MaxFilter); editor lost the Soft-edge slider (crisp brush), gained a Seam panel (Softness + Mask grow + Blend-mode), a live DPR-backed seam preview (`render.mjs::_seamAlphaCanvas`), a switchable preview color (`Pixaroma.Inpaint.PreviewColor`, display-only), "Reset all to default", and Target-snaps-to-multiple. Pattern 5 above is current.
> **DONE — softness rework PART 1 (functional, Option B), committed on `Ioan` 2026-06-16 (separate commit after the safe fixes; absolute-px softness, chosen by the user over a relative/% redesign).** `compute_region` context expand now uses `max(context_px, blend)` (added `blend:16` to DEFAULTS + the merge_params int-list; `node_inpaint_crop.py::run` sets `params["blend"]=clamp(softness)` BEFORE `apply_inpaint_crop`; MIRRORED in `geometry.mjs` GEO_DEFAULTS + `ctx=max(context_px,blend||0)`; the editor already feeds `this.params.blend` via `_recomputeRegion`, so the editor crop box grows with softness for free). `_blur_alpha` DROPPED the rect-edge guard + the `max(..,mb)` core clamp - the feather now always reaches 0 before the crop edge because the crop grew (opaque inside by construction). Fixes BOTH the original ghost AND the v2 HARD-STEP-at-high-softness (a big feather no longer can't-fit). So the editor seam tint now MATCHES the stitched result — the user no longer over-sets softness. NO cache needed: `_draw` runs only on strokes / slider-drags / load (NOT idle mouse-move - the brush cursor draws on a separate canvas), and the capped buffer keeps the DT ~2-3ms. The pure fn is node-tested (`D:\Claude Tests\_inpaint_seam_test.mjs` - inside=1, smoothstep falloff to 0 at k px, monotonic, empty/full); the full canvas path is eye-verified. Docs: `inpaint-crop-math.md` §4 + Patterns 3 & 5 updated. > **DONE — round-2 safe fixes (committed on `Ioan` 2026-06-16, a separate commit BEFORE the softness rework; no behavior change beyond fixing the bugs).** (1) OOM: `compute_region` keep-mode now runs the min_size short-side bump FIRST and the max_size clamp LAST (hard ceiling), so an extreme-aspect (thin-line) mask can't blow the output past max_size (the short side may then end < min_size - acceptable). Mirrored in `geometry.mjs`. (2) FORCE-STRETCH: force mode now RE-IMPOSES the source aspect == `out_w/out_h` AFTER the image-bound clamp (shrink the over-long axis to the largest aspect-correct rect that fits), so an oblong image is no longer stretched. Mirrored in `geometry.mjs`. Both locked by harness tests `test_keep_mode_respects_max_size` + `test_force_mode_preserves_aspect`; `docs/inpaint-crop-math.md` §1 updated.

### Preview Image Pixaroma Patterns (do not regress)

These patterns were hard-won during the May-2026 batch + save-mode upgrade. Several of them generalize to ANY canvas-rendered preview node, so re-read this section before building a similar widget.

1. **Native PreviewImage layout pattern: constant `minHeight` + fit-contain in available space — DO NOT mutate node size based on image aspect.** ComfyUI's `useImagePreviewWidget` returns `{ minHeight: 220 }` and inside `draw()` computes `scale = Math.min(slotW/imgW, slotH/imgH, 1)` to fit the image in WHATEVER rect the user-resized node grants. We tried two earlier approaches that both failed: (a) `computeSize` returns aspect-driven height + `node.setSize` to fit on frame load — caused FLICKER on every resize because `fitNodeToWidgets` snapped height back mid-drag; (b) cap aspect-driven height at a max — still snapped on aspect changes (portrait → landscape left empty grey). The only correct pattern is: `computeSize` returns a constant minimum; `draw` reads `Math.max(MIN_H, node.size[1] - y)` for actual height; image is fitted inside via min-scale. User can resize freely both directions, image always fits, no flicker. See `js/preview/index.js` `layoutImgStrip` + `createStripWidget.computeSize` + `createStripWidget.draw`.

2. **`widget.mouse()` only fires for clicks INSIDE the widget's `computeSize` bounds — clicks in the extended-draw area below need a node-level `onMouseDown` fallback.** This is the consequence of (1): when the strip widget reports `minHeight: 220` but draws at e.g. 600px (tall node), LiteGraph's click router uses the 220 figure for hit-testing. Clicks below that line aren't routed to `widget.mouse()` at all. The fix is a DUAL CLICK PATH: a shared `handleStripClick(node, lx, ly)` helper called from BOTH `widget.mouse()` AND `nodeType.prototype.onMouseDown` (which fires when no widget claimed the click). Both use the same hit-rects from `_pixaromaCells`. Without the dual path, big nodes lose click on bottom thumbnails. The earlier finding that `widget.mouse() returning false doesn't fall through to node.onMouseDown` is true ONLY when LiteGraph routed the click to the widget in the first place — for clicks outside widget bounds, `node.onMouseDown` does fire, hence the fallback works.

3. **Pixaroma-specific UI key (`pixaroma_preview_frames`) instead of `ui.images` — required to disable LiteGraph's native image strip rendering.** Returning `ui.images` from a Python node causes ComfyUI to populate `node.imgs` and draw its own image strip below the widgets. Our custom strip would render on top → double rendering. Save Mp4 set the precedent (`pixaroma_videos`); we follow it. Frontend listens to `api.addEventListener("executed", ...)`, reads `detail.output.pixaroma_preview_frames`, and renders. Cross-version node-id resolution — `app.graph.getNodeById(detail.node)` first, then `parseInt(detail.node, 10)` if string — required because Vue passes the node id as a string while legacy passes a number (Save Mp4 pattern, used in multiple Pixaroma nodes).

4. **Preview persistence across workflow tab switching: store frame metadata on `node.properties`, hydrate on `onConfigure` AND `queueMicrotask(onNodeCreated)`.** This is the **standard Pixaroma persistence pattern for any preview-style node** — IMPORTANT to reuse for future preview nodes that need to survive Vue tab switches. Frame URLs (filename + subfolder + type), selected index, expanded state — all live on `node.properties.pixaromaXxx`. LiteGraph serializes `properties` to workflow JSON natively, so persistence is automatic. On node restoration, a small `restoreFromProperties(node)` helper re-loads HTMLImageElements from the persisted URLs. Wire it from BOTH (a) `queueMicrotask(() => restoreFromProperties(this))` inside `onNodeCreated` (Vue Compat #8 — `onNodeCreated` fires BEFORE `configure()` so we defer past it), AND (b) `nodeType.prototype.onConfigure` (belt-and-braces for paths that bypass the microtask). The function is idempotent via an early-return guard `if (node._pixaromaFrames?.length) return`. Use this exact pattern for any new node where the user shouldn't lose preview state when switching tabs. The temp/ PNG files survive workflow switching (cleared only on ComfyUI restart) — for permanent persistence across restarts, write to output/ via the save_mode pattern below.

5. **Hover state on canvas-drawn buttons: read `app.canvas.graph_mouse` inside `draw()`, no extra wiring.** LiteGraph already redraws on every pointermove, so reading `graph_mouse` per draw call gives free per-frame hover detection. Convert to node-local: `mx = graph_mouse[0] - node.pos[0], my = graph_mouse[1] - node.pos[1]`. Hit-test against the same rect the click handler uses. Branch the fill/stroke style on hover. This is what native ComfyUI does for the X close button on PreviewImage — no DOM widget needed. We use `BRAND` (orange) on hover and dark gray otherwise. The cursor change (CSS `cursor: pointer`) is optional and conflicts with LiteGraph's own cursor management — skip unless really needed.

6. **`save_mode` widget pattern (preview / save combo) for nodes that should be both preview and save destinations.** Adds a required combo widget and `prompt: PROMPT, extra_pnginfo: EXTRA_PNGINFO` hidden inputs in `INPUT_TYPES`. Default to `preview` for preview-first nodes. In `save` mode, iterate the entire batch, call `folder_paths.get_save_image_path(prefix, output_dir, w, h)` once for the base counter, then save each frame as `{name}_{counter+i:05}_.png` with embedded metadata via the shared `nodes/_save_helpers._build_pnginfo`. Same pattern Save Mp4 uses (with `save` / `preview` routing to output/ vs temp/). For backwards compat: a workflow saved before the `save_mode` widget existed loads with the default — verified for Preview Image Pixaroma. Same pattern can be applied to other preview nodes wanting save-on-execute.

7. **Save-to-Disk filename auto-increment via per-node session offset (`_pixaromaDiskOffset`).** `folder_paths.get_save_image_path` only sees files in ComfyUI's `output/`, not the user's chosen disk location. So every Save-to-Disk click would suggest the same filename. Fix: track a per-node click counter (`node._pixaromaDiskOffset`), bump after each successful save, apply via `bumpFilenameCounter("img_00002_.png", offset)` to the server-suggested name. Reset to 0 on each `executed` event (new run = fresh counter base from output/). NOT persisted across workflow saves — accepted trade-off since disk save locations are user-chosen anyway.

8. **`_safe_prefix(s)` sanitizer — relative-import shared helper module + fallback contract (None means "use the default prefix").** Lives in `nodes/_save_helpers.py`. Returns the sanitized prefix, or `None` if input is unrecoverable. Every caller falls back so a save never crashes: `node_preview.py` + both preview routes use `_safe_prefix(s) or "Preview"`, the XY Plot save route uses `or "xy_plot"`. **Sanitizes, does not reject — and it is a DENYLIST, not an allowlist (flipped June 2026 after the Korean `filename_prefix` report).** Per segment, ONLY Windows-illegal chars (`< > : " | ? *` plus control chars) are replaced with `_` (repeated `_` collapsed; edge whitespace, edge `_`, and trailing dots/spaces stripped — Windows itself silently strips trailing dots/spaces at create time, so stripping keeps the reported path identical to what lands on disk); Windows reserved device names (CON, PRN, AUX, NUL, COM1-9, LPT1-9 — bare or with any extension, any case) get a `_` suffix so the OS can't hard-error mid-run. EVERYTHING else passes through verbatim — non-Latin scripts (`프로젝트/테스트/이미지` saves like native), accented letters, spaces, dots — matching native SaveImage, which does no character filtering at all (its only guard is folder_paths' "stay inside output/" commonpath check, which still runs after ours on every save path). The old `[^A-Za-z0-9_\-%]` allowlist dissolved an all-Korean prefix to nothing → silent "Preview" fallback in the output root, and mangled mixed ones (`te 스 st` → `te_st`). An upstream filename wired into `filename_prefix` (e.g. `Bunny WithCubes - Copy.png`) now stays verbatim. Path segments are separated by `/`; `\\` normalized to `/` (Windows convenience). Returns `None` only for: non-string, empty input, length > 256, leading `/`, any segment that is literally `..` (path traversal), or nothing usable left (e.g. `???`). **`scripts/save_prefix_check.py` locks all of this (31 cases, prints `PREFIX PASS`) — re-run it after ANY change to the sanitizer.** **`%` is permitted in segments** so two layers of token expansion both work: (a) **VHS-style `%date:FMT%`** is expanded BEFORE sanitization by `_expand_date_tokens` (Java-style codes `yyyy yy MM dd HH mm ss`, two-pass sentinel swap to avoid `yyyy`/`yy` collision, bad format strings leave the token literal so the user can spot the typo); (b) **native ComfyUI tokens** `%year% %month% %day% %hour% %minute% %second% %width% %height%` survive sanitization as literal `%`-delimited segments and are expanded later by `folder_paths.get_save_image_path.compute_vars`. Net result: `%date:yyyy-MM-dd%/images/fish_` and `%year%-%month%-%day%/img` both work. Path traversal is impossible: explicit `..` segment rejection, ComfyUI does its own `os.path.commonpath` check after its expansion, and Java date codes can only emit digits. `nodes/_save_helpers.py` is imported via `from .nodes._save_helpers import _build_pnginfo, _safe_prefix` (relative import, package-aware) — NEVER `from nodes._save_helpers` because that collides with ComfyUI's top-level `nodes.py`. The `nodes/` directory is an implicit namespace package (no `__init__.py`) and that's fine.

9. **Tracking the "active" preview node for global keybindings (`_activePreviewNode`).** Module-scope `let _activePreviewNode = null`. Set on click that enters expanded mode; clear on X close, Esc, OR `nodeType.prototype.onRemoved` (so deleted nodes don't dangle a reference and prevent GC of their loaded images). Window-level `keydown` listener routes ←/→/Esc to whichever node is active, with `INPUT/TEXTAREA/contentEditable` exclusion so the user can still type. Use capture-phase (`true` 3rd arg to `addEventListener`) so we preempt ComfyUI's canvas-pan keybindings. Same pattern can be reused for any other node that needs document-level keyboard control while focused.

10. **Inline expand-in-place over fullscreen lightbox.** Native PreviewImage doesn't dim the canvas behind a lightbox — clicks on the strip thumbnail expand THE SAME widget into a single-image view (X close, counter, dimensions). Stay inside the node body. Two earlier attempts went different directions and were rejected by the user: (a) full-viewport overlay with 0.92 black backdrop ("not fullscreen"); (b) viewport-centered card without backdrop ("not like that, like preview imafge from comfyui does"). The final shape is: same strip widget, two render modes via `_pixaromaExpanded` flag, all controls drawn on the node canvas. Click-image-to-advance gives quick batch flipthrough without exiting expanded mode.

11. **Self-heal `node.size` at draw time, not via `onResize`.** The buttons widget's `draw()` checks `node.size[0] < MIN_W` (and `MIN_H`) and clamps + `setDirtyCanvas` if so. `nodeType.prototype.onResize` is also installed but cannot be relied on alone: Vue Compat #13 says `onResize` doesn't reliably fire for DOM-widget resizes, AND Align Pixaroma's resize intercept (Align Pattern #6) writes `node.size` directly via cursor delta and bypasses the hook entirely. Symptom this prevents: drag the node smaller than `MIN_W` and the button row visually overflows the right edge of the node frame (buttons clamped to `BTN_MIN_W` × 4 still need >= `MIN_W` of node width, but `widget_width` was honestly small). The draw-time clamp self-heals on the next frame regardless of which path got us there. One-frame flash is acceptable. Pattern generalises: any Pixaroma node whose widgets have a hard minimum width should clamp in draw, not (only) onResize. Same lesson applies to Copy / Open buttons added in May 2026 — they raised `MIN_W` from 224 to 314, and saved workflows that already have smaller saved sizes self-correct on first paint.

12. **Copy + Open buttons act on the SELECTED frame, just like Save.** Native ComfyUI's right-click menu on Preview Image Pixaroma shows "Copy (Clipspace)" — that's ComfyUI's INTERNAL clipspace (for paste-into-LoadImage flows), NOT the OS clipboard. There is no native "Copy Image" or "Open Image" because we use the custom `pixaroma_preview_frames` UI key (Pattern #3) so `node.imgs` isn't populated the way the native menu code expects. The Copy button fills that gap via `navigator.clipboard.write([new ClipboardItem({"image/png": pngBlob})])`. Force the blob MIME to `"image/png"` (some servers return `image/x-png` and `ClipboardItem` is strict). Browser support: Chrome / Edge / Firefox 127+ / Safari 16+ — fall back to a toast if `navigator.clipboard?.write` or `ClipboardItem` is undefined (don't crash, don't pretend it worked). The Open button does `window.open(frame.url, "_blank", "noopener")` — `noopener` so the new tab can't reach back into the ComfyUI window via `window.opener`, and we toast "Popup blocked" if `window.open` returns null. Both honour `node._pixaromaSelectedFrame` so the user gets the frame they clicked, not the first or last (a real upgrade over native which only ever sees one image).

13. **Save Disk / Save Output embed the EXECUTION-time workflow, not the live graph - and the meta payload MUST be NaN-sanitized.** Two linked facts learned May-2026 (GitHub-style report: "saved image reproduces a DIFFERENT image when dragged back"). (a) The frontend Save buttons originally called `app.graphToPrompt()` at CLICK time. With KSampler `control after generate: randomize`, ComfyUI bumps the seed widget to the NEXT random value the instant a run finishes - so by the time the user clicks Save, the live graph has the WRONG seed, and the embedded workflow reproduces a different image. The auto-save (`save_mode=save`, Python) was correct because it embeds the PROMPT/EXTRA_PNGINFO handed to it AT EXECUTION (the real seed). Fix: `node_preview.py` returns the execution-time `{prompt, workflow}` in the ui payload (now embedded on the first frame entry as `_pixaroma_meta` per Pattern #16, was previously a separate `pixaroma_preview_meta` key); `js/preview/index.js` captures it on the `executed` event into `node._pixaromaExecPrompt`/`_pixaromaExecWorkflow` (RUNTIME ONLY - never persist to `node.properties`, it would recursively bloat the saved workflow with a copy of itself); `resolveSaveMeta(node)` returns the captured exec metadata, falling back to live `graphToPrompt()` only when no run happened this session. (b) **CRITICAL: any node `ui` payload sent over the websocket MUST contain only strict-JSON-safe values.** PROMPT carries `is_changed: [NaN]` for this node because `IS_CHANGED` returns `float("nan")`. `NaN` is invalid JSON, so the frontend `JSON.parse` of the entire `executed` message throws (`api.ts` WebSocket onmessage) and the WHOLE message is dropped - preview frames AND save metadata both lost (symptom: preview shows a stale/404 frame, buttons silently fall back to live graph). `node_preview.py` `_json_safe()` recursively replaces NaN/Inf with `None` before adding the meta to the `ui` dict. RULE for any future node that puts richer data in its `ui` payload: sanitize non-finite floats first; never assume PROMPT/widget values are JSON-clean.

14. **`ui.images` is the ONLY signal that triggers the Media Assets panel refresh.** Discovered May-2026 (GitHub issue #43, "Pixaroma nodes break the Assets panel"). ComfyUI's Media Assets panel (both the web frontend's right-sidebar Assets tab AND ComfyUI Desktop's media browser) listens for `ui.images` on the `executed` event as its "a new output file was just saved, refresh the list" signal. It does NOT watch the filesystem - any node that saves to `output/` but uses a custom ui key (like our pre-fix `pixaroma_preview_frames`, or Save Mp4's `pixaroma_videos`) is invisible to the Assets panel even though the file is sitting right there in `output/`. Without emitting `ui.images`, users perceive Pixaroma's save nodes as "breaking" Assets - same symptom whether the panel never updates or other plugins' saves don't show either. Fix: when a Pixaroma node actually writes to `output/`, ALWAYS emit `ui.images` (alongside or instead of any custom key). Skip this for nodes writing to `temp/` (Assets ignores temp files by `type` filter, so emitting there is pointless refresh churn). **Save Mp4 has the same latent bug for output-mode videos** - if a user reports the asset panel not showing saved mp4s, port this fix there too (mp4s probably go in `ui.videos` or similar; verify with the bundle).

15. **The native `$$canvas-image-preview` widget gate is `node.imgs?.length`, NOT a hardcoded node-type list - lock node.imgs to [] to suppress.** Verified by grepping `dialogService-DSBgqcNn.js` for `showCanvasImagePreview` in May-2026: `t.imgs?.length && !t.widgets?.find(e=>e.name===`$$canvas-image-preview`) && addCustomWidget(t, {type:'IMAGE_PREVIEW', name:'$$canvas-image-preview'})`. The auxiliary `supportsVirtualCanvasImagePreview` set (PreviewImage / SaveImage / GLSLShader) is for SUBGRAPH proxy widgets specifically, NOT for the auto-add gate. So as soon as Pixaroma Preview emits `ui.images` (per Pattern #14), ComfyUI populates `node.imgs` and adds the native preview widget BELOW our custom strip widget - producing a duplicate thumbnail. Setting `node.imgs = null` in the `executed` handler does NOT remove the widget once it's been added (the `find()` short-circuit means it persists for the lifetime of the node). The fix is Prompt Reader Pixaroma Pattern #2: `Object.defineProperty(this, "imgs", {configurable: true, get(){return []}, set(_v){}})` in `onNodeCreated`. The getter always returns an empty array, so the `node.imgs?.length` gate fails forever and the native widget never gets added in the first place. Side-effect: right-click menu items that read `node.imgs[0]` (Copy Clipspace, Open Image) become no-ops for our node - already the case before this fix since we never populated `node.imgs`, so no regression. Always probe the existing descriptor first (`getOwnPropertyDescriptor(node, "imgs")`); if `configurable === false`, `defineProperty` throws and you'd silently lose the suppression. Log a one-time warning so a future Vue-frontend change surfaces in the console.

16. **`outputs_count` (Assets stack badge) counts EVERY dict item across EVERY list-keyed ui array - use one ui key per mode and embed extras as fields.** Server-side math lives in `comfy_execution/jobs.py::get_outputs_summary`: iterate `outputs.items()`, for each `(media_type, items)` where `items` is a list (and media_type isn't `animated`), iterate items and `count += 1` per dict (with a special branch for text/3D-string items). The result becomes the asset's `outputs_count`, which the frontend reads as `getStackCount(asset)` → renders the "N" stack badge when N > 1. Pre-fix we emitted THREE ui keys for one save: `pixaroma_preview_frames` (1 frame dict) + `pixaroma_preview_meta` (1 meta dict) + `images` (1 frame dict, same data as frames) → outputs_count = 3 → confusing "3" badge on a single saved PNG. The fix that keeps the count at 1: emit ONLY ONE ui key per mode (`ui.images` in save_mode=save for Assets refresh per Pattern #14, `ui.pixaroma_preview_frames` in preview mode), and embed the metadata as an EXTRA FIELD on the first frame entry (`results[0]["_pixaroma_meta"] = {prompt, workflow}`). The server counts ARRAY items, not nested fields - so 1 list with 1 dict counts as 1, regardless of how many extra fields the dict carries. Frontend's `ResultItemImpl` constructor in `dialogService-DSBgqcNn.js` only copies known fields (filename / subfolder / type / mediaType / nodeId) so the extra `_pixaroma_meta` field is silently ignored by the asset card rendering, but is still present in the raw output dict that our JS executed handler reads via `frames[0]._pixaroma_meta`. RULE for any future Pixaroma save-node design: NEVER emit the same data under both `ui.images` AND a custom mirror key; NEVER emit metadata as a separate ui list-key. One key, one entry per file, extras-as-fields.
- `_safe_path()` in `server_routes.py` — validates all file paths stay within `PIXAROMA_INPUT_ROOT`
- IDs validated against `^[a-zA-Z0-9_\-]+$` regex (max 64 chars)
- Base64 payloads capped at 50 MB
- Note sanitizer (`js/note/sanitize.mjs`) — allowlist-based. Anything user-reachable (link insert, code-view HTML edit, paste) must round-trip through `sanitize(html)` before being written to the DOM or saved. Class allowlist covers only Pixaroma-specific classes; style allowlist covers only `color`, `background-color`, `text-align`; href allowlist is `http:`, `https:`, `mailto:`.

### Prompt Stack Pixaroma Patterns (do not regress)

These patterns were hard-won during initial implementation. Re-read before touching `js/prompt_stack/` or `nodes/node_prompt_stack.py`.

1. **Wire mode (per-row input dot aligned with row) was attempted and abandoned — DO NOT bring it back.** The original spec wanted each wire-mode row to show an input slot dot aligned vertically with its row. Empirical testing showed the Vue frontend completely IGNORES `slot.pos` overrides: setting `node.inputs[i].pos = [0, y]` updates the property but the dot stays at the natural top-of-slot-area position. CLAUDE.md Vue Compat #16 documents the same issue for `getConnectionPos`. There is no public API in this ComfyUI build that moves input dots away from the natural top-stack layout. If you ever need per-row wired input, the only working pattern is the Switch Pixaroma approach: canvas-paint the entire row UI (no DOM widget) so the canvas-paint Y can be set to whatever ComfyUI uses for the natural input slot Y. That's a fundamental architectural change to Prompt Stack and is NOT worth the rework.

2. **`stripLegacyWireSlots(node)` runs in BOTH `onNodeCreated` and `onConfigure`** — the original wire-mode implementation pre-declared 16 optional `wire_N` STRING inputs in Python's `INPUT_TYPES`. Those wires got serialized into saved workflows. The current Python no longer declares them, but loaded workflows still carry the stale `wire_N` entries in `node.inputs[]`. The cleanup strips any `wire_*`-prefixed input slot defensively so old workflows render clean. Without it, the node shows 16 useless input dots on the left.

3. **`measureContentHeight(root)` sums children `offsetHeight`, NEVER `root.scrollHeight`** — same trap as Load Image Pattern #4. ComfyUI stretches `root.offsetHeight` (and therefore `scrollHeight`) when the node has slack height, creating a feedback loop: report stretched height as minimum → ComfyUI keeps it stretched → next measure reports it bigger again → node grows unboundedly. The fix is to ignore the stretched root and sum children's intrinsic heights, plus CSS row-gap and root padding.

4. **`growNodeToContent` is one-way (only grows), `fitNodeToContent` is two-way (used on delete only).** Default behavior is one-way grow so a user's manual resize-bigger sticks. Only explicit "compacting" actions (row delete) call `fitNodeToContent` to shrink the node back. Don't make the typing path or the toggle path call `fitNodeToContent` — that would shrink the node mid-edit if the textarea text got shorter, which feels wrong. `fitNodeToContent` also enforces a floor of `DEFAULT_H` so single-row states still look intentional.

5. **Initial textarea `autoGrow` MUST defer to `requestAnimationFrame`** — `scrollHeight` returns 0 for elements that aren't in the DOM yet. `renderRows` creates the textarea, calls `attachTextareaEditor` (which calls `autoGrow`) BEFORE `root.appendChild(rowEl)`. If `autoGrow` runs synchronously here, every re-render collapses previously-grown rows back to CSS min-height. The fix: `requestAnimationFrame(() => { autoGrow(taEl); ... })` so the measure happens after layout. Bug class this prevents: "I typed 6 lines into row 1, clicked Add row, and now row 1 looks empty / 1 line tall".

6. **DOM widget MUST have `canvasOnly: true`** — per Vue Compat #15. Without it, the entire row stack also renders in the right-sidebar Parameters tab AND its draw call corrupts the node body layout. Set inside the 4th-arg options object of `addDOMWidget(name, type, element, options)`.

7. **Drag-to-reorder bails on input/textarea/button targets** — `attachDragHandlers` in `interaction.mjs` checks `e.target.tagName` at `dragstart` and bails (via `e.preventDefault()`) if the target is `INPUT` / `TEXTAREA` / `BUTTON`. This preserves native text-selection inside the textarea and native click behavior on the ON pill / label / X delete. Without this guard, dragging to select text inside a row triggers a reorder.

8. **`pixConfirm()` themed dialog — never reach for `window.confirm()`** — lives in `interaction.mjs`. CSS classes `.pix-ps-confirm-backdrop` / `.pix-ps-confirm-box` / `.pix-ps-confirm-title` / `.pix-ps-confirm-msg` / `.pix-ps-confirm-actions` / `.pix-ps-confirm-btn[.primary]` in `render.mjs`. Returns `Promise<boolean>`. Esc / backdrop click / Cancel = false; Enter / OK = true. Used for the row-delete confirm. Same UX rule as Note Pattern #7: don't yank the user out to browser chrome when a themed inline dialog will do.

9. **Separator setting uses a fresh ID `Pixaroma.PromptStack.SeparatorText`** (NOT `Pixaroma.PromptStack.Separator`) because the original was a `combo` type that was migrated to a `text` type mid-development. ComfyUI persists setting values keyed by ID; reusing the old ID left users seeing stale combo values like `"Custom..."` in the new text field. Renaming gave a fresh slate. If you ever change the type of a setting in this project, rename the ID at the same time. The `onChange` resets to default `, ` when the user clears the field (a make-shift "reset to default" since ComfyUI's settings panel has no per-field reset button). `resolveSeparator()` interprets `\n` (backslash + n) and `\t` typed in the field as newline / tab characters.

10. **Default sizing constants are tuned to single-row-fresh-node**: `DEFAULT_W = 400`, `DEFAULT_H = 180`. The grow/fit allowance is `contentH + 50` (`~30 title + ~10 body top padding + ~10 body bottom padding`). If you change row visuals materially (taller row chrome, bigger ON pill, etc.) these constants should be revisited so a single-row default still feels snug. Default size only applies to fresh nodes (the `if (node.size[1] < DEFAULT_H)` guard preserves saved workflow sizes).

### Prompt Multi Pixaroma Patterns (do not regress)

These patterns were hard-won during initial implementation. Re-read before touching `js/prompt_multi/` or `nodes/node_prompt_multi.py`.

1. **`app.queuePrompt` patch must fall through immediately when no Prompt Multi node exists in the graph.** The patch wraps a hot path (every Run click); when no PM node is present, the patch does ONE graph walk via `findFirstPromptMultiNode` then calls `_origQueuePrompt(num, batchCount)` unchanged. Do NOT add any logging, telemetry, or per-node iteration above this early-return — same idiom as Switch and Resolution's `graphToPrompt` patches.

2. **`activeIndex` is the ABSOLUTE position in `rows[]`, not the enabled-filtered position.** The queue loop reads `enabledRowsWithIndex(node)` (which preserves absolute indices) and writes `state.activeIndex = entry.index` per iteration. The `graphToPrompt` hook then does `state.rows[activeIndex].text`. Confusing absolute vs filtered indices breaks the per-row text injection when there are disabled rows between enabled ones (e.g. rows `[ON, OFF, ON]` → enabled indices are `[0, 2]`, not `[0, 1]`).

3. **0-enabled toast MUST bail without calling `_origQueuePrompt`.** Returning `undefined` (no original call) is the correct behavior — the user toggled everything off, they meant to skip. Calling the original with the saved `activeIndex` would launch one stale run, which is worse than no-op.

4. **Per-row enqueue failures are logged and skipped, not aborted.** If one iteration of the loop throws, the loop continues with the remaining rows. Defensive — a transient ComfyUI queue error on row 2 shouldn't kill rows 3-5. Logs the error and presses on.

5. **State persistence: `activeIndex` is saved but not relied on at load.** The next Run's queue loop overwrites it before any prompt is captured, so the value sitting in the saved workflow JSON is whatever the last loop iteration left behind. Don't add migration logic that "restores" `activeIndex` from saved state — it's transient.

6. **Multiple Prompt Multi nodes: only the first drives count.** `findFirstPromptMultiNode` walks `app.graph._nodes` top-level first, then recurses into subgraphs. The first hit wins for the queue count. Other Prompt Multi nodes in the same workflow each use their own `activeIndex` (whatever was set by user interaction or the last run). Document this if a user reports the second PM node "isn't running multiple times".

7. **`Prompt Multi ≠ Prompt Stack` — DO NOT add a separator setting.** Prompt Stack has `Pixaroma.PromptStack.SeparatorText`; Prompt Multi has nothing equivalent because it doesn't join. If a future contributor adds one, the node's semantics would silently shift toward Prompt Stack territory and confuse users.

8. **Toast helper has a fallback for old ComfyUI builds.** `showNoEnabledToast` tries `app.extensionManager?.toast.add()` first (modern API), then falls back to a hand-rolled brand-bordered `<div>` banner with `setTimeout` cleanup. Don't remove the fallback — `extensionManager.toast` is not present on the older Easy Install builds users still run.

9. **Empty enabled rows are silently skipped at queue time — `enabledRowsWithIndex` filters by BOTH `enabled` AND `text.trim()`.** Deliberate UX call (May 2026): an ON row with no text is treated the same as OFF. If you drop the text filter, every empty placeholder row queues a meaningless workflow run with an empty string downstream (CLIP Text Encode etc. happily renders nothing). The textarea placeholder and Python DESCRIPTION both call this out — keep them aligned with the filter's actual behavior. The 0-enabled toast message reads "Enable at least one non-empty prompt to run." which covers both the all-disabled AND the all-empty cases without needing two branches.

10. **Two outputs (text + prompts) are ALWAYS visible — do NOT try to dynamically swap output slots based on mode.** Tried (May 2026) and abandoned: in List mode, renaming `node.outputs[0]` to "prompts" + PIXAROMA_PROMPT_LIST and removing slot 1 looks right visually but routes the WRONG Python return through the wire. Python's `RETURN_TYPES = ("STRING", PIXAROMA_PROMPT_LIST)` is positional — slot 0 always carries the STRING `active_text`, slot 1 always carries the LIST. Frontend rename does not reroute. Symptom of the bug: From List nodes downstream receive `active_text` (a single string) instead of the list, but isinstance(prompts, list) might still pass if you hit the wrong type-check timing. Plus `slot.label` is set from RETURN_NAMES at registration and is sticky — the rename only takes if you ALSO set label (not conditionally). The architectural fix: always show both outputs, let the user wire whichever they need, and use the mode pill purely to gate queue loop behaviour. Trade-off accepted: two output dots on the node's right side instead of one. Anyone tempted to "make it cleaner" via dynamic slot juggling should re-read this paragraph first.

11. **Mode toggle controls ONLY queue loop behaviour, never output visibility.** Queue mode -> the queuePrompt patch loops once per enabled non-empty row. List mode -> the patch short-circuits to a single `_origQueuePrompt(num, batchCount)` call. The user-facing pill labels are `Queue Text` (telling the user "wire the text output") and `List Prompts` (telling the user "wire the prompts output"), but the OUTPUTS themselves stay constant. The hint text under the pills also names which output to wire. If you ever feel tempted to add "auto-detect what's wired and pick the mode", DON'T — explicit toggle has predictable behaviour, auto-detect surprises users (this exact discussion happened May 2026 and the user picked explicit).

12. **`graphToPrompt` hook ships BOTH `activePrompt` AND `rowTexts` regardless of mode.** Python doesn't care which mode is set at submit time — it just gets both fields and the executor picks whichever output the workflow JSON wires. The JS hook always populates `rowTexts` as the enabled-non-empty rows in display order (NOT all rows — the filter mirrors queue-mode behaviour so a downstream From List index of 1 maps to the first ENABLED row, never an OFF or empty one). Including the `mode` field in the JSON is for future safety only — current build doesn't read it on the Python side.

13. **PIXAROMA_PROMPT_LIST is a Pixaroma-private wire type.** Custom string identifier (NOT a built-in ComfyUI type) so only nodes that explicitly opt into the exact name connect. Currently used by Prompt Multi's `prompts` output and Prompt From List's `prompts` input. If you add a new third-party list-source node, declare your output as the same string and the wire will connect. If you ever rename it, sync BOTH places at once (Python type tuple in both node files + the PIXAROMA_PROMPT_LIST constant in both Python files — keep the duplicated definition in sync, it's deliberate to avoid a cross-file import chain).

14. **`findFirstPromptMultiNode` / `findFirstPromptPackNode` only return a node that actually DRIVES the queue: active (mode !== 2 muted, !== 4 bypass) AND has at least one output connection.** GitHub issue #39: a leftover Prompt Multi / Prompt Pack node sitting empty on the canvas (unwired, or muted/bypassed) was intercepting EVERY Run via the `app.queuePrompt` patch and aborting the whole workflow with its "Enable/Paste at least one prompt to run" toast - even when the node had nothing to do with the workflow being run. The find helpers now skip non-participating nodes so the patch falls through to a normal `_origQueuePrompt` single run. The connected-and-empty case (node wired up but no prompts) STILL toasts - that's the legitimate "you forgot to type prompts" warning. The toast/bail only fires for a node that is genuinely part of the run. Connection check = any `node.outputs[i].links?.length > 0`; mode check = `node.mode !== 2 && node.mode !== 4`. Same fix duplicated in `js/prompt_pack/core.mjs` (findFirstPromptPackNode) and `js/prompt_multi/index.js` (findFirstPromptMultiNode); keep them in lockstep. Note the graphToPrompt hooks are already safe (a disconnected node never appears in the pruned prompt output, so it's never injected).

15. **Any `app.queuePrompt` patch MUST forward ALL arguments (`...args`), or the per-node "Execute to selected output nodes" (partial execution) silently runs the FULL graph.** ComfyUI's frontend signature is `queuePrompt(number, batchCount = 1, queueNodeIds)` — the THIRD arg `queueNodeIds` is the list of output-node ids for partial execution (the blue ▶ "Execute Node" button, right-click "Execute" on a node). Verified in the bundle: `queuePrompt(e,t=1,n){ ...this.queueItems.push({number:e, batchCount:t, queueNodeIds:n, ...}) }`. The Prompt Multi (`js/prompt_multi/index.js`) and Prompt Pack (`js/prompt_pack/index.js`) `app.queuePrompt` wrappers originally declared `function (num, batchCount)` and forwarded only those two — so `queueNodeIds` was dropped and EVERY partial-execution click ran the entire workflow, for any user with the plugin installed (the wrappers patch `app.queuePrompt` at load time, independent of whether a Prompt node is on the canvas). Reported May-2026 (someone pressed "Execute Node" on an audio Preview node and got a full run; reverting to 1.3.35 fixed it). Fix: wrapper signature is `async function (...args)`; every fall-through / list-mode call is `_origQueuePrompt.apply(app, args)` (Multi) / `_origQueuePrompt(...args)` (Pack); the per-row/per-prompt LOOP builds `const loopArgs = args.slice(); loopArgs[1] = 1;` and calls `_origQueuePrompt.apply(app, loopArgs)` — overriding ONLY batchCount, preserving `number` + `queueNodeIds` + any future args. This mirrors what every `app.graphToPrompt` hook in the project already does (they all use `...args`). RULE: never declare a fixed-arity wrapper around a ComfyUI app/api method you don't fully own — always `(...args)` + `.apply`/spread, because ComfyUI adds trailing params across versions. The `api.queuePrompt` patch in `js/prompt_pack/index.js` already follows this (it uses `...args`); only the two `app.queuePrompt` patches had the bug.

16. **TWO `app.queuePrompt` queue-driver patches (Prompt Multi + Prompt Pack) CHAIN and MULTIPLY when both nodes are present — guarded by the shared `js/shared/queue_drivers.mjs` lock + a Switch-aware participation check.** Reported May-2026 (Discord "Prompt Multi Node Bug"): a workflow with Prompt Pack (3 prompts), Prompt Multi (3 rows), and Prompt Stack all wired into ONE Switch Pixaroma produced 9 image generations instead of 3 (another user: 4 prompts → 16). TWO compounding causes:
    - **Multiplication.** Each driver patches the GLOBAL `app.queuePrompt` once at module-load time (per node TYPE, NOT per node instance), and the patches CHAIN: each wrapper's `_origQueuePrompt` is the next plugin's wrapper. Load order is alphabetical, so `prompt_multi` patches first (inner) and `prompt_pack` patches second (outer). With both a Multi node AND a Pack node active+connected, clicking Run makes Pack's wrapper loop M times and each iteration re-enters Multi's wrapper which loops N times → M×N submissions (3×3 = 9). There was NO re-entrancy guard. Fix: `js/shared/queue_drivers.mjs` exports a module-singleton lock — `isQueueLoopActive()` / `runQueueLoop(fn)` (Multi uses this) / `beginQueueLoop()`+`endQueueLoop()` (Pack uses these inside its existing batch-counter try/finally). Each wrapper's FIRST line is `if (isQueueLoopActive()) return _origQueuePrompt(...)` — so whichever driver starts looping first holds the lock and any nested driver falls through to a single pass-through call. The lock is released in a `finally` so a thrown submission can't wedge Run into permanent pass-through.
    - **Inactive Switch branch.** A Switch Pixaroma routes only ONE input per run, but the participation checks (`isMultiNodeDriving` / `isPackNodeDriving`, Pattern #14) only asked "do I have an output link?" — so every driver wired into the Switch counted as driving, regardless of which input the Switch routes. Fix: `feedsOnlyInactiveSwitch(node)` in the shared module returns true when EVERY output link of the node lands on a `PixaromaSwitch` input whose 1-based slot index ≠ the Switch's `properties.switchState.activeIndex`; both `isXNodeDriving` predicates now AND in `!feedsOnlyInactiveSwitch(node)`. So only the driver on the Switch's active input drives the queue. It FAILS OPEN (returns false → participates) on any uncertainty: missing graph, unresolved link (`graph.links` may be a Map — Vue Compat #3), non-numeric activeIndex, or a thrown error — better to over-run than silently drop the user's prompt. A driver that also feeds a non-Switch target (or the Switch's active input) keeps participating normally; this is purely additive to the issue-#39 active+connected gate.
    - Net result for the reported workflow: Switch active = Solo/Pack → only Pack loops (3 runs of Pack's prompts); active = Duo/Multi → only Multi loops (3 rows); active = Stack → neither loops (1 run of Stack's joined text). Matches "leave only one in the Switch and it works". Prompt Stack is NOT a driver (it never patches `app.queuePrompt`, just joins text), so it never multiplied. ONLY these two nodes loop the Run button; audit with `grep "app.queuePrompt ="` (the `api.queuePrompt` patch in `prompt_pack/index.js` is capture-only, no loop). Any NEW queue-driver node MUST import and use this shared guard (both the lock and, if it can feed a Switch, the suppression check), or it will reintroduce the multiplication.

### Prompt From List Pixaroma Patterns (do not regress)

Tiny picker node, ~80 lines of Python, no custom JS. Pairs with Prompt Multi's `prompts` output in List mode.

1. **No widget customisation — ships as plain ComfyUI native widget rendering.** The whole point is "small node, one number input, no chrome". Do NOT add a custom DOM widget, a fancy index spinner, or anything else that bulks it up. If the user wants more controls, they're better served by piling small From List nodes than by stuffing one big picker.

2. **Out-of-range index returns `""` instead of raising.** Mirrors Prompt Multi's "be forgiving" stance: a workflow with a mistyped index still RUNS (downstream nodes will surface the empty-prompt issue with their own behaviour). Raising would block the whole queue submission with an opaque traceback.

3. **`isinstance(prompts, list)` check is mandatory.** Defensive guard for the case where someone wires a non-list source into the input despite the type system (legacy workflows, manual JSON edits, or a future bug in Prompt Multi). Returning `""` cleanly is better than crashing on `prompts[idx0]` with a TypeError mid-queue.

4. **The Prompt Reader walker chases `prompts` → upstream Multi, indexes `rowTexts`.** Per Prompt Reader Pattern #12-13 family. The walker special-cases `PixaromaPromptFromList`: reads the `index` widget value from the prompt JSON, follows the `prompts` link tuple `[upstream_id, slot_idx]` to the upstream node, confirms it's a `PixaromaPromptMulti`, and returns `rowTexts[index-1]` from the upstream's hidden state. If the upstream is anything ELSE (some future list-source node), the walker returns None — only Multi → From List recovery is supported. Adding a new list-source node? Mirror the rowTexts-on-hidden-state pattern, then extend `_pix_prompt_from_list_resolve` to recognise that node's class_type.

### Mute Switch Pixaroma Patterns (do not regress)

These invariants were hardened over three rounds of audit (18 agent reviews) before shipping. Re-read before refactoring `js/mute_switch/` or `nodes/node_mute_switch.py`.

1. **Mute ONLY the directly wired upstream node, NOT the whole upstream chain.** This is the deliberate v2 semantic. ComfyUI's executor is lazy — when KSampler is muted, anything downstream of KSampler that has no other consumer is skipped automatically, AND anything upstream of KSampler that nothing else needs is also skipped automatically. So setting mode=2 on ONE node (the directly wired one) effectively skips the whole branch at execution time — but only THAT node greys out on the canvas, which is the desired visual. The OLD design (walk the whole BFS upstream + refcount-spare-shared-nodes) was removed in v2 because it was both more complex AND visually noisier. Do NOT reintroduce a BFS walker.

2. **Cascade ONLY through inner Mute Switches.** `cascadeMuteSet` (`upstream.mjs`) recurses ONLY when the target is itself a `PixaromaMuteSwitch`. For all other node types it adds and stops. This is what makes "outer switch picks a group" work: muting the inner switch's row also mutes everything wired INTO the inner switch (including its leaf nodes). Visited-set seeded with the calling switch's id prevents self-mute and cycle infinite-loops.

3. **`applyAllMuteSwitches` is graph-wide, not per-switch.** Every Mute Switch in the graph contributes to a single `wantMuted` union map. Any switch's "OFF" wins. Each `applyMuteState` call funnels through `applyAllMuteSwitches`. Do NOT refactor to per-switch isolation — that loses cross-switch coordination and breaks the "outer overrides inner" semantic.

4. **`originalModes` is distributed across switches with "first to save wins" ownership.** The first switch to save a node's original mode owns that entry. When that switch is deleted (`restoreAllOnRemove`), it (a) restores its own entries, (b) re-runs `applyAllMuteSwitches(graph, excludeId)` — a surviving switch that still wants the node muted will re-mute it and take over ownership of the original. Do NOT centralize `originalModes` to a single switch or to `app.graph` — distributed ownership survives node deletion cleanly.

5. **Always save the original mode when first muted by us, EXCEPT save 0 as a fallback when `n.mode === targetMode` already.** `core.mjs:393-409` saves in `originalModes` regardless of whether we need to change the mode (so the entry exists for restore). BUT when the node was already at target mode at save time (somebody else muted it — user manual right-click, previous buggy save, leftover from a deleted Mute Switch), save 0 instead of n.mode. Saving the actual n.mode (2) would silently re-mute on untoggle, orphaning the user's intent. Saving 0 means untoggle reliably returns the node to active. The companion **self-heal sweep (Pattern #16)** catches any orphans that slip through.

6. **All serialized writes are diff-gated to prevent dirty-on-load (Vue Compat #18).** This includes `slot.pos`, `slot.label`, `slot.name`, `outputs[0].label`, `outputs[0].pos`, `node.size[0/1]`. Compare `if (cur.x !== x || cur.y !== y) cur = [x, y]` patterns. Do NOT add an unconditional write to serialized state anywhere on the load path — `onConfigure → restoreFromProperties → normalizeSlots` is the load funnel, and any unconditional write there pops "Save Changes?" on plain open+close.

7. **`node.size[0] = DEFAULT_W` ONLY in `setupNode`, never in `normalizeSlots`.** Width-clobber on load was the original dirty-on-load source. `setupNode` runs in `onNodeCreated` BEFORE `configure()`, so its DEFAULT_W write is overridden by the saved size on workflow load — affecting only fresh-on-canvas drops.

8. **Phantom `out` output uses custom type `PIXAROMA_MUTE_CHAIN`, NOT `*`/ANY.** This is the runtime safety net — LG's type system blocks the user from wiring `out` into non-Mute-Switch inputs (CLIPTextEncode, KSampler, etc.) that would crash receiving the `(None,)` Python return value. Mute Switch's own `ANY` inputs accept `PIXAROMA_MUTE_CHAIN` because ANY/`*` matches anything. Schema migration in `normalizeSlots` upgrades old workflows with `outputs[0].type === "*"` to the new type (one-time legacy dirty, acceptable).

9. **`pruneOrphanedOriginalModes` runs at the top of every `applyAllMuteSwitches`** to drop entries whose upstream node was deleted from the graph. Without this, accumulating stale entries eventually bloat the saved JSON. `pruneOrphanedOriginalModes` only touches the calling switch's entries, but every switch gets pruned each apply pass.

10. **Empty `muteSwitchOriginalModes` is deleted at the end of `applyAllMuteSwitches`** to avoid serializing `"muteSwitchOriginalModes": {}` for switches that have nothing to track. The dict is lazy-recreated on the next write.

11. **Configure-replay gate `_pixMsConfiguring` + load-wide `isGraphLoading()` BOTH gate `onConnectionsChange`** (Vue Compat #17 + #19). The per-node flag covers `onConfigure`; `isGraphLoading()` covers the graph-level link-restore that fires AFTER each node's `onConfigure` has cleared its flag. Skipping either gate lets the connection-replay overwrite saved state.

12. **`_pixMsPatched` flag on `nodeType.prototype` prevents hot-reload exponential wrapping.** Same pattern Switch Pixaroma uses. When `beforeRegisterNodeDef` fires twice for the same nodeType (extension hot-reload), the flag short-circuits.

13. **Inline label editor uses `installGraphUndoGuard` (Vue Compat #6).** Without it, Ctrl+Z inside the DOM input would escape to ComfyUI's Vue undo (via `requestAnimationFrame`-scheduled `loadGraphData`) and could tear the underlying node out from under the open editor.

14. **Node IDs are stringified consistently** — `nodesById[String(n.id)]`, `wantMuted.set(String(id), targetMode)`, etc. LG node ids can be numbers or strings; explicit `String()` avoids surprise when comparing across `Map` keys vs object keys (object keys auto-stringify on read; Map keys don't).

15. **`STATE_VERSION` + `_migrateState` is the SINGLE entry point for schema upgrades.** Currently v1, no-op. When v2 ships, add the migration branch to `_migrateState` rather than scattering defaults across readers.

16. **Self-heal sweep at the end of `applyAllMuteSwitches`** catches orphaned mutes — nodes wired to an ON row that are currently at `mode != 0` but no switch tracks them in `originalModes`. When found, set `mode = 0`. Catches: external mutes the user forgot about (right-click → Set Mode → Mute then wired to a row whose pill is ON), state corruption from previous buggy saves (the bug class this fix exists for), cross-switch consistency violations. **Only ON rows are swept**; OFF rows want their upstream muted by design. Mute Switch IS the source of truth for nodes wired to it — if the pill says ON, the canvas matches.

17. **Bulk row toggles via right-click menu (`Enable all rows` / `Disable all rows`).** Implemented as a one-time `LGraphCanvas.prototype.getNodeMenuOptions` patch guarded by `_pixMsMenuPatched` (same hot-reload hygiene as `_pixMsPatched` on `nodeType.prototype`). Both items always appear in the menu for discoverability but are `disabled: true` in Single mode (the "exactly one ON" invariant rules out all-ON and all-OFF) and when there are no wired rows. The callbacks call `setAllRowsEnabled(node, true|false)` which only flips WIRED rows (unwired rows can't meaningfully mute anything), gates on `state.selectMode === "multi"`, and triggers a single `applyMuteState` at the end. Per-row pill clicks still work the same — this is just a shortcut for the common "flip everything" case.

### XY Plot Pixaroma Patterns (do not regress)

These were hardened over four agent-review waves + live testing (June 2026). Re-read before touching `js/xy_plot/` or `nodes/node_xy_plot.py`.

1. **It is the THIRD `app.queuePrompt` / `app.graphToPrompt` queue-driver (after Prompt Multi + Prompt Pack) and MUST use the shared `js/shared/queue_drivers.mjs` lock.** First line of the `queuePrompt` wrapper is `if (isQueueLoopActive()) return _origQueuePrompt.apply(app, args)`; the N×M loop runs inside `runQueueLoop(...)`. Forward `...args` (preserve `number` + `queueNodeIds` so partial-execution "Execute Node" still works); only override `args[1]` (batchCount) to 1 per cell. `findFirstXyNode`'s participation gate mirrors the other drivers: active (mode !== 2/4) + `imageWired(n)` + `computeCounts().hasPlot` + `!feedsOnlyInactiveSwitch(n)`. A non-participating XY node MUST fall through to a normal run, never block it (an unwired node with axes set used to `return` undefined and silently killed every Run — that regression is fixed by putting `imageWired` IN the gate).

2. **Per-cell value injection happens in the `app.graphToPrompt` hook (Pattern #9), keyed off a NON-serialized runtime cursor `node._pixXyRun`.** The driver sets `_pixXyRun = {sessionId, xi, yi, cols, rows, xValue, yValue, xLabels, yLabels, ..., seedMap}` synchronously before each awaited `_origQueuePrompt` (same proven timing as Prompt Multi — graphToPrompt runs synchronously inside queuePrompt and reads the cursor). Cleared in a `finally`. Do NOT store the cursor on `node.properties` (would dirty the workflow, Vue Compat #18). The hook no-ops when `_pixXyRun` is null, so normal runs (and every plugin user's normal workflows) are untouched; it's wrapped in try/catch and always returns the original `result`.

3. **`injectAxis` OVERRIDES a wired input (replaces the link array with the cell's literal).** The user explicitly chose that input as an axis, so a converted-to-input widget (e.g. Empty Latent Image's `width` wired from Resolution Pixaroma) must be swept by replacing its `[nodeId, slot]` link with each cell's value — exactly the Switch-style prompt mutation. Do NOT re-add a "skip wired inputs" guard (that made wired-input sweeps silently do nothing → identical cells). The one exception: text **find-&-replace** can't run on a wired text (we don't have the string), so it warns and skips. `findPromptEntry(out, nodeId)` resolves the target: direct `out[String(nodeId)]`, else match a `"subgraph:id"` key by tail.

4. **Seed lock keeps each sampler's OWN seed constant across cells — it does NOT homogenize them.** `captureSeedMap` snapshots every seed/`noise_seed` widget keyed by `String(node.id)`; `applySeedLock` matches by EXACT prompt key (NOT tail-id — tail-id collides across subgraph scopes). Auto-disabled when an axis targets a seed (`seedTargeted`). Never overwrites a wired seed (`typeof !== "object"`).

5. **Python owns ALL grid rendering; JS just shows the PNG as an `<img>`.** `node_xy_plot.py` accumulates cells server-side in `_SESSIONS` keyed by a per-plot `sessionId` (created on-absent — a retried (0,0) cell must NOT wipe accumulated cells), guarded by a module `threading.RLock` (`execute` on the worker thread races the `/restyle` + `/save` routes on the aiohttp thread; assemble under the lock, do file I/O outside it). `_assemble_grid` is wrapped in try/except in `execute` so a malformed state falls back to passthrough, never crashes the run. `cols`/`rows` capped at `_MAX_DIM=100` (matches JS `MAX_AXIS_VALUES`), out-of-range cells skipped, labels sliced to dims. Evicted sessions delete their temp grid PNG. The grid `<img>` is `max-height:360px` capped so a tall (many-row) grid can't grow the node unbounded; a legacy one-shot shrink corrects an over-tall size carried over from the Nodes 2.0 renderer (gated `!isVueNodes() && !grid && size > want+120`, so no churn/dirty on correctly-sized nodes).

6. **Save Output embeds the EXECUTION-time prompt/workflow (Preview Pattern #13/#16), not the live graph.** Python attaches `_pixaroma_meta = {prompt, workflow}` to the grid frame; JS caches it on the `executed` event (`node._pixXyExecPrompt/_pixXyExecWorkflow`, runtime-only) and `doSaveOutput` uses it (falls back to live `graphToPrompt()` only if no run happened). Routes `/pixaroma/api/xy_plot/{save,restyle}` validate `session_id` via `_SAFE_ID_RE`/`_MAX_ID_LEN`, the theme against {dark,light,mono}, and `_is_path_under` the cells subfolder; `/save` reads cells via the lock-protected `snapshot_session_cells`.

7. **The picker must NOT list hidden/internal state widgets.** `classifyWidget` skips `$$`-prefixed, `pixaroma_*`-typed, `w.hidden`, `type === "hidden"`, and statically-`canvasOnly` widgets — otherwise a node's serialized-state STRING widget (Note's `note_json`, Label's `label_json`, hidden via `hideJsonWidget` which sets `w.hidden = true`) shows up as a pickable "text" target with its raw JSON. Same family: a combo axis filters `raw.checked` against the widget's current live options so a sampler/checkpoint removed after a model update isn't injected.

8. **`readState` identity stability + in-place resets.** `readState`/`backfillAxis` mutate the axis objects in place (never replace `s.x`/`s.y`/`raw` with fresh objects) and `selectChoice` resets `axis.raw` IN PLACE — because value-field handlers capture `axis.raw` by reference; swapping the object reintroduces the "editing one axis clobbers the other" bug. The picker popup is a module singleton; `closePopupIfOwner(node)` (not bare `closePopup`) is called from `onRemoved` so deleting one node doesn't close another's open picker.

9. **Number-axis rounding uses the widget's declared `precision`, NOT the `step` (June 2026; refined after integer ranges came out fractional).** ComfyUI tags every number widget with `precision` = decimals allowed (0 = integer width/height/steps/seed/batch_size, 1 = cfg, 2 = denoise) AND carries the REAL increment in `step2` (width 16, cfg 0.1), while the plain `step` option is ×10-inflated (width 160, cfg 1.0) and unreliable. `classifyWidget` captures `precision`; `roundToStep(v, step, precision)` rounds to `precision` when present. History (two passes): the FIRST fix derived decimals from `max(stepDecimals, valueDecimals)` to stop floats truncating (`cfg 5,6,7.1` -> `5,6,7`; `denoise 0.05,0.1` -> `0.1,0.1`; `cfg 0-1 x4` -> `0,0,1,1`), but that then made INTEGER ranges fractional (`width 512-1024 in 4 steps` -> `512, 682.66666667, 853.33333333, 1024`, because an interpolated value's own decimal count is 8). Switching to `precision` fixes BOTH: width/height/steps/seed stay whole, cfg keeps 1 decimal, denoise 2, and `cfg 1-2 x4` tidies to `1, 1.3, 1.7, 2`. Fallback (precision missing - old saved axis / non-ComfyUI widget) is the `max(stepDecimals, valueDecimals)` cap-8 logic. `axis.precision` is set in `selectChoice` and self-healed each render in `renderValueArea` (so a reloaded pre-fix axis still rounds right). `step2` (the real increment, captured as `axis.realStep`) drives a PER-AXIS **Snap** toggle (`axis.snap`, default ON): `resolveAxisValues(axis)` reads `axis.snap` and snaps each number value to the nearest multiple of `realStep`, then re-rounds to precision - so width/height land on clean multiples (512-1024 x4 -> 512, 688, 848, 1024) while cfg/steps/denoise are no-ops (their step equals the precision unit). PLACEMENT: the Snap toggle renders INSIDE the number axis's value area, in the free space beside the Range/List segment (a `.pix-xy-moderow`), so it adds NO node height; and it shows ONLY when snapping would actually change values (`realStep > 10^-precision`, i.e. width/height), not for cfg/steps. (A single global toggle in the options row was tried first but wrapped to a 4th line and added height - user-rejected; per-axis-in-the-value-area is the placement.) Snapping never changes the value COUNT (no dedupe), so `computeCounts`/`axisReady` stay consistent with the driver. The injection path (`index.js` `injectAxis`), Python (`node_xy_plot.py`), and the grid labels all consume the resolved list untouched, so `roundToStep` is the SINGLE precision authority for number axes. (Verified with a throwaway Node harness asserting int/float/range/fallback cases.)

10. **Per-axis reset (`resetAxis` in core.mjs) clears ONE axis in place; the global Reset still wipes everything.** `resetAxis(node, axisKey)` blanks just `state[axisKey]`, mutating the existing axis object IN PLACE (Pattern #8's aliasing rule), leaving the other axis + toggles + theme + any shown grid intact. It's exposed through the node's `handlers.resetAxis` (so node-fitting stays in `index.js`, like `handlers.reset`) and rendered as a small `↺ Reset` in each axis header, shown only once a setting is picked (nothing to reset on an empty axis). It calls `fitNode` (grow OR shrink) so the node tightens after a tall value area collapses - a user action, so it can't trip dirty-on-load (#18). Must be threaded into BOTH the live `makeHandlers` object AND the `_pixXyRenderOnly` handler object, or the button is inert right after a workflow load.

### Image-picker node patterns (do not regress)

Any Pixaroma node that picks an image from `input/` via ComfyUI's `image_upload: True` widget is an "image-picker node". Current members: **Load Image Pixaroma** (`js/load_image/`, `nodes/node_load_image.py`) and **Prompt Reader Pixaroma** (`js/prompt_reader/`, `nodes/node_prompt_reader.py`). The two share an upload-button + hidden-native-combo + custom-dropdown + (now) prev/next arrows surface. If you add a third such node (e.g. a future "Load Mask Pixaroma"), follow every rule below or you will regress hard-won fixes.

1. **`image_upload: True` creates TWO widgets — hide BOTH, plus any future siblings.** See Load Image Pattern #1 below for the full rationale. The standard recipe is `hideNativeImageCombo(node)` in `js/load_image/ui.mjs` / `js/prompt_reader/index.js`: iterate every widget, set `hidden=true`, `computeSize=()=>[0,-4]`, `options.canvasOnly=true`, hide DOM `element` / `inputEl`. Re-run inside `requestAnimationFrame` because Vue may DOM-render a widget AFTER `nodeCreated`. Returns the `image` combo so the picker UI can read/write `.value`.

2. **Programmatic `widget.value` writes do NOT fire ComfyUI's `image_upload` setter — every pick path must also call `updateNativePreview(node, filename)` (or its node-local equivalent).** Otherwise the bottom-of-node preview stays stuck on the previously-loaded file. See Load Image's `api.mjs::updateNativePreview` for the canonical implementation: `new Image()` → `node.imgs = [img]` on load. Mirror it in any new image-picker node.

3. **`updateNativePreview` MUST race-guard with a per-node monotonic request id.** Rapid pick-A-then-B picks queue two concurrent fetches; `img.onload` fires in **LOAD order**, not call order. Without a request id, a slow A landing after a fast B silently clobbers `node.imgs` back to A. Pattern: bump `node._pix<NodeShort>PreviewReqId` at the top of every call, capture the value into `myReq`, and bail in both `onload` and `onerror` if `node._pix<NodeShort>PreviewReqId !== myReq`. This was part of the issue #38 hardening.

4. **Subfolder paths must be split on the last `/` before building the `/view?` URL.** ComfyUI's `input/` folder can hold subfolders; the combo values include path-prefixed names like `Studio1/cat.png`. The `/view` endpoint expects `subfolder` + `filename` as SEPARATE query params - sending the slash inside `filename=` and an empty `subfolder=` silently 404s on some Comfy builds. Use `splitFilenameSubfolder(path)` (or the local `splitPath` equivalent) and pass both params.

5. **Dropdown popup MUST group by subfolder.** Users on shared input folders accumulate dozens of subfolders. Flat list = unscannable. Group by subfolder with small `.pix-*-popup-section` headers ("root", "Studio1", "Renders" ...), items show the bare filename only, hover `title` carries the full path so it stays discoverable. Selected item should auto-scroll into view on popup open (the user's current image is what they want to find first, especially when navigating with prev/next).

6. **Defensive `_pix<NodeShort>SelectedFilename` cache + sync at submission time (issue #38 hardening).** Whenever the user picks a new image (dropdown / arrow / upload / paste / drop / native drag-drop), write the filename to a per-node cache `node._pix<NodeShort>SelectedFilename`. Seed it from `imageWidget.value` in three places: the wrapped `imageWidget.callback` (covers native drag-drop), the initial setup after `hideNativeImageCombo` returns (covers configure-already-landed-by-then), and `onConfigure` (covers workflow reload). For nodes whose Python contract reads the image filename from `widget.value` (which is what `image_upload: True` makes natively serialise) **patch `app.graphToPrompt` to re-sync `widget.value = cached` and `entry.inputs.image = cached` just before submission** if they drifted apart. Reason: Vue's configure replay can fire at unpredictable moments (tab switch, autosave then load) and silently restore an older saved value over the user's in-session pick. The cache + graphToPrompt fix prevents that drift from leaking into the submitted prompt. Load Image is the reference implementation; Prompt Reader uses the same cache pattern but does not need the graphToPrompt sync because the workflow only sends the image filename to the Python node which reads metadata server-side (no prompt-time injection needed). **CRITICAL (issue #50): the graphToPrompt override MUST exempt `clipspace` values.** ComfyUI's Mask Editor (and "Copy/Paste (Clipspace)") write the EDITED image - with the painted mask baked into its ALPHA channel - to `input/clipspace/clipspace-mask-*.png` and point the image widget there, often WITHOUT firing the widget callback. So the cache still holds the pre-edit filename, and the blind `widget.value !== cached -> revert to cached` sync reverts the widget to the maskless original; the backend loads it, finds no alpha, and the MASK output comes back BLANK (user-visible: "I drew a mask, saved, and the Load Image node produces no mask"). Fix: in the graphToPrompt hook, when the live submitted value matches `/clipspace/i`, ADOPT it into the cache (`node._pixLiSelectedFilename = live`) and skip the override entirely; only apply the cache-revert for non-clipspace values. This works whether or not the Mask Editor fires the callback. The Python side was already correct (it reads `1 - alpha` like native LoadImage) - the mask was being lost purely because the clipspace filename never reached the backend. **Follow-up (Copy/Paste Clipspace):** the same root cause also breaks "Copy (Clipspace)" -> "Paste (Clipspace)", but the `/clipspace/i` exemption does NOT catch it - when you copy an OUTPUT image from another node and paste it onto Load Image, ComfyUI's `pasteFromClipspace` first block assigns `widget.value = "<name>.png [output]"` (no "clipspace" substring) with NO callback, so the cache stays stale and the override reverts to the old file (user-visible: node preview shows the pasted image but the OUTPUT is the previous one). The general fix is a **value setter on the image widget** (installed in `setupLoadImageNode`): `Object.defineProperty(imageWidget, "value", {...})` chains any existing descriptor and, on every write, updates `node._pixLiSelectedFilename = v` UNLESS `isGraphLoading()` (a load-time write is Vue config-replay and must not touch the cache, preserving #38). This catches every external write path (Mask Editor, both clipspace blocks, native drag-drop) regardless of whether a callback fires, so the cache is always the user's latest deliberate pick and the override only ever fires to undo a genuine config-replay drift. Guarded by try/catch + a `desc.configurable` check so a future non-configurable widget value can't throw.

7. **Prev / next arrows on a dedicated `pickByOffset(node, offset)` helper with PageUp/PageDown shortcuts.** Visual flip-through, matches native ComfyUI LoadImage. Wrap at both ends. Buttons disable when `values.length < 2`.
